# Executive Summary

Between Ponds is a genuinely novel mobile concept with strong emotional differentiation and no direct competitor. The advisory panel's consensus is that the round is **fundable — with corrections**. Three structural errors in the pitch materials must be resolved before investor meetings.

<div class="rpt-kpi">
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat warning"><span class="kpi-value">€0.04</span><span class="kpi-label">Stated ARPDAU</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat"><span class="kpi-value">600,000</span><span class="kpi-label">Stated DAU Target (Y2)</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat error"><span class="kpi-value">€8.76M</span><span class="kpi-label">Implied ARR at Stated ARPDAU</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat accent"><span class="kpi-value">1.37M DAU or €0.091 ARPDAU</span><span class="kpi-label">Required to Hit €20M Target</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat success"><span class="kpi-value">Yes — with corrections</span><span class="kpi-label">Panel Fundability Verdict</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat purple"><span class="kpi-value">High</span><span class="kpi-label">Creative Vision Coherence (all 6 art frames)</span></div>
</div>

## The Three Structural Errors

**1. The Revenue Math Is Broken**

€0.04 ARPDAU × 600,000 DAU yields approximately **€8.76M ARR** — not the implied €20M+ target. The gap is not a rounding error; it is a factor of **2.3×**. Closing it requires either 1.37M DAU (2.3× the stated target) or an ARPDAU of €0.091 (2.3× the stated rate). Neither path is addressed in the pitch materials. This must be corrected before any investor meeting.

**2. The Monetization Model Is Missing Its Primary Revenue Engine**

The cosmetic-only model lacks a **gifting mechanic**. Sky: Children of the Light demonstrated that gifting — not personal cosmetic purchase — is the primary revenue engine for gift-economy games. Players buy gifts for strangers, not skins for themselves. Between Ponds' entire design philosophy is built around giving; the monetization model does not exploit this alignment.

**3. The Game Lacks a Proprietary Emotional Phrase**

The creative vision is singular and coherent — the highest-confidence finding in the review, confirmed across all six art frames. However, the game does not yet have a **proprietary phrase for its emotional register** that travels across all four launch markets (Germany, Japan, United Kingdom, Brazil). Without it, the pitch deck cannot make investors feel what the game is before they play it.

## Panel Assessment

<span class="rpt-badge success">Fundable</span> The concept is the right kind of risk. The pitch materials are not.

*See [Monetization Analysis], [Competitive Landscape], and [Recommendations] for detailed remediation paths.*

---

# Literature Landscape

The advisory review draws on five primary research traditions and a set of documented historical case studies. Together they form the evidential foundation for the panel's findings across domain boundaries.

## Research Traditions

<div class="rpt-bars">
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Haiku therapy / expressive writing</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill success" style="width:85%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">High relevance</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Gift economy theory (Mauss)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill success" style="width:80%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">High relevance</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Nishikigoi cultural heritage</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:75%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Med–High</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Dark pattern / FOMO mechanics</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:70%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Med–High</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Grief and games research</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:65%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Medium</span></div>
</div>

### Haiku Therapy and Expressive Writing

The haiku therapy tradition in Japan dates to the 1970s. The literature documents that writing haiku about negative life events increases creativity and decreases illness orientation; the formal constraints of haiku "make it possible to structure chaotic thoughts." Poetry therapy provides comfort and boosts mood during stress, grief, and trauma by funnelling overwhelming experience "into a concise, beautiful little nugget." This research base directly supports Between Ponds' core design thesis — the haiku constraint is doing **documented therapeutic work**, not merely aesthetic work.

### Gift Economy Theory (Mauss, 1925)

Marcel Mauss's *The Gift* establishes the foundational framework: gift exchange in community settings carries three obligations — to give, to receive, and to reciprocate. **Between Ponds deliberately breaks the third obligation.** Fourcade & Kluttz (2020) introduce the concept of a "Maussian bargain" — aestheticising gift-giving while embedding the pleasure of accumulation. Research on digital gifting in KakaoTalk, LINE, and WeChat (2025) confirms that platform architecture shapes which cultural norms around reciprocity are activated.

### Kigo System: A Precision Instrument, Not a Vocabulary List

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>Kigo are not decorative seasonal markers — they are a codified repository of cultural associations. When Between Ponds' on-device dictionary suggests kigo to players, it potentially injects this cultural freight into messages composed by players who have no awareness of what they are loading.</p><footer>Haiku Pedagogy Expert · Confidence: 0.85</footer></blockquote>

The World Kigo Database project documents the challenge of kigo translation across climate zones. A single Japan-centric kigo list for four markets creates exactly the kind of cultural flattening the Kyoto Koto Foundation relationship is supposed to prevent. Two defensible paths: **(a)** a genuine haiku education layer explaining what each kigo means before a player selects it; **(b)** a simplified regional kigo system that strips the cultural charge and makes seasonal words function as simple seasonal markers. Half-measures — a suggestion engine with no cultural annotation — may produce more cross-cultural misfire than no kigo system at all.

### Nishikigoi Cultural Heritage

Key verified facts: koi keeping in Japan dates to the Heian period (794–1185); formalized breeding of ornamental koi began in the Edo period (1603–1868); Yamakoshi Village (Niigata) is the acknowledged origin of the nishikigoi art form and was recognised as a Japan Agricultural Heritage site in 2015. The kohaku variety (visible in art frames 01 and 05) was fixed as a variety by 1917. **Critically**, nishikigoi is a specific practice associated with Niigata Prefecture hobbyist culture — not a universal Japanese symbol. Using koi as a universal "Japanese kindness" symbol risks homogenising a diverse cultural tradition.

The Kodomo no Hi (Children's Day, May 5th) koinobori cultural association — koi-shaped windsocks associating koi with family spirit — means that Drift Away mechanics may activate **family-dissolution anxiety associations** in Japanese players, a framing entirely absent from the game bible.

### Dark Pattern and FOMO Mechanics Literature

The *darkpattern.games* taxonomy and peer literature define the core dark pattern as "implied threat of loss to drive return engagement." Tamagotchi death mechanic research shows that pet death created distress in children crossing clinical thresholds. NetEase Ananta (2025) analysis demonstrates that removing FOMO mechanics required compensation through rich content to maintain DAU — the substitution cost is non-trivial. Animal Crossing's villager goodbye mechanic generated a 400k+ subreddit community response, indicating the emotional magnitude of comparable loss mechanics in non-coercive games.

### Grief and Games Research

Frontiers in Psychology (2023) finds that games provide "unique meaning-making experience to bereaved players by affording agency to actively reconstruct their narrative of loss." Between Ponds' Memorial Pond **inverts** this finding — it removes agency rather than affording it. The literature supports using games as protective spaces for confronting loss; it does not support removing the player's role in the ritual.

## Regulatory and Legal Reference Base

| Instrument | Application |
|---|---|
| EU Unfair Commercial Practices Directive (2005/29/EC) | Drift Away asset removal without adequate disclosure |
| DSA Article 25 (EC final guidelines, 2025) | Artificial urgency and fear-of-loss design |
| UK CMA 2023 guidance | Loss-of-progress mechanics conditioned on engagement |
| EU Digital Content Contracts Directive (2019/770) | Digital asset removal from digital content contracts |
| GDPR Articles 4(1), 5(1)(e), 6, 7(3), 8, 17 + Recital 26 | Memorial Pond, city-level location, age consent, erasure |
| UK Online Safety Act (in force July 2025) + Ofcom 2025 guidance | Children's Risk Assessment, age assurance, illegal content |

## Historical Case Studies: Japanese Aesthetics in Western Games

| Title | Year | Developer | Outcome | Lesson |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Ghost of Tsushima | 2020 | Sucker Punch / Sony | Tepid initial Japanese reception; eventual success | Asset review without framing review is insufficient |
| Journey | 2012 | thatgamecompany | Recognised as culturally authentic | Structural integration beats decorative borrowing |
| Okami | 2006 | Capcom (Japanese) | Universally cited as most authentic | Internal cultural production sets the baseline |

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>The legitimacy of a consultancy arrangement depends not on its formal structure but on the scope of the brief. If the Foundation's brief is limited to reviewing specific assets without addressing the broader cultural framing, the formal arrangement provides legitimacy without catching the most important cultural missteps.</p><footer>Games Historian · Confidence: 0.75</footer></blockquote>

**Assessment of the Kyoto Koto Foundation arrangement**: The structure — veto rights, 1% net revenue, permanent co-author credit, annual audits — is substantially more robust than most historical consultancy arrangements. The veto right is the critical element: cases where consultants had advisory input but no veto consistently resulted in studios overriding cultural concerns under commercial pressure. The remaining gap is one of *scope*: the Foundation's brief must be broad enough to address framing (koi as universal Japanese symbol vs. koi as specific Niigata hobbyist tradition) not only individual assets.

### Japanese Seasonal Calendar as Cultural Organising Principle

Japanese aesthetic tradition organises social, ritual, and emotional life around the four seasons (四季, *shiki*) in ways structurally different from Western seasonal awareness. Koi hibernation in the game is biologically accurate — koi enter torpor below ~10°C — and Japanese koi keepers are deeply aware of this cycle. This biological accuracy is the game's deepest cultural authenticity signal.

However, the seasonal system's application to the Southern Hemisphere creates a structural inequity: for Brazilian players, kigo that ground a poem in real seasonal experience will arrive at Japanese ponds in the opposite season. The kigo's claim to temporal situatedness — its entire cultural function — is false to the receiver. **Proposed fix**: display both sender's and receiver's seasonal context when a haiku is read ("written in winter, received in summer"). This reframes seasonal inversion as evidence of distance travelled — itself a culturally Japanese solution, acknowledging the gap rather than papering over it.

*See [Compliance Matrix], [Ethical Considerations], [Findings by Domain], [Visual Analysis], [Theoretical Framework], and [Competitive Landscape] for cross-domain applications of this research base.*

# Live Service Roadmap

Between Ponds' cosmetic-seasonal monetisation model generates ongoing live operations requirements that the current six-person team is structurally unable to meet at launch. The roadmap below details the required cadence, the hemisphere asymmetry risk window, and the secondary market timeline — three independent operational challenges that interact to create a single high-risk period in **December 2027 – February 2028**.

## Year 1 Live Ops Requirements

Five functions must be staffed before global launch. None are currently documented in the team structure:

| Function | Description | Risk if Unstaffed |
|---|---|---|
| Seasonal cosmetic cadence | 4 major seasonal themes/year + 12–16 à la carte items | Revenue miss; Audience C churn |
| Cohort analytics | Drift Away reactivation rate tracking; D7/D30/D90 | Misread designed seasonality as permanent decline |
| Network density monitoring | Reply rate per haiku in months 1–3 | Memory Wall viability signal missed; no course-correction window |
| Multi-jurisdictional compliance | Ongoing monitoring across DE, JP, UK, BR | Regulatory action in any of four markets |
| Secondary market intelligence | Rare pattern economy emergence tracking | Two-tier player population forms without studio awareness |

<span class="rpt-badge error">Critical Gap</span> **Minimum hire required before launch: 1 live ops / data analyst.** Year 1 compliance budget estimate: €150,000–€300,000.

---

## Hemispheric Season Asymmetry

The game's real-calendar seasonal mechanic creates structurally unequal day-one experiences across launch markets. The Northern hemisphere launch (Germany, Japan, UK) in Autumn 2027 means the first winter hibernation arrives **8–12 weeks post-install** — before the majority of players have experienced the cherry-blossom hero-shot conditions depicted in the App Store listing.

| Market | Launch Season | First Winter | Hero Shot Alignment |
|---|---|---|---|
| Germany / Japan / UK | Autumn 2027 | 8–12 weeks post-install | <span class="rpt-badge error">MISALIGNED</span> — cherry blossoms in listing; bare branches in-app |
| Brazil (temperate south) | Spring / Summer 2027 | 6+ months post-install | <span class="rpt-badge success">ALIGNED</span> — spring conditions match hero shot |
| Brazil (equatorial) | Dry season variant | N/A — no clear seasonal milestone | <span class="rpt-badge warning">NOT APPLICABLE</span> — mechanic is a placeholder |

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>The equatorial design is the weakest sentence in the game bible — an acknowledged design gap delegated to the future. Equatorial players receive no clear seasonal milestone, are excluded from Northern-winter/Southern-summer cross-breeding rare patterns, and experience the game's central impermanence metaphor in muted form.</p><footer>Live Service Analyst · Evidence: High</footer></blockquote>

**Operational risk window**: December 2027 – February 2028. All three Northern hemisphere markets simultaneously enter low-activity state. Only Brazil remains in active summer. This is the studio's **first investor-metrics trough** and is likely to be misread as permanent decline rather than designed seasonality. Live ops must prepare explicit documentation of this window for investors before launch.

### Recommended Fix: Biome-Based Seasonal Triggering

Replace hemisphere-based with biome-based seasonal triggering. Brazil's wet/dry cycle is cinematically rich — monsoon flooding, receding waters, species emergence. Designing the pond around that cycle rather than treating it as a degraded Northern winter would convert an acknowledged design gap into a distinct regional experience. Academic framing: Laura op de Beke (2025/2026, *Time and Society*) identifies hemisphere-only seasonal design as "cultural hegemony of the temperate Northern hemisphere" that marginalises tropical seasonal experience.

---

## Soft-Launch Timing Risk

Portugal (Northern Hemisphere) + New Zealand (Southern Hemisphere) is the correct hemispheric pairing for soft launch. However, one full seasonal cycle before global launch is **insufficient to model churn seasonality with statistical confidence**. The specific gap: the December–February Northern winter trough will occur only once in the soft-launch window. A single data point cannot distinguish designed hibernation behaviour from structural retention failure.

**Recommendation**: Extend soft-launch observation to 18 months (two full Northern winters) or accept that the first global winter trough will be a live experiment with real investor visibility.

---

## Secondary Market and Rare Pattern Economy

<div class="rpt-kpi">
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat warning"><span class="kpi-value">4–8 months</span><span class="kpi-label">Secondary Market Emergence (post full launch)</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat accent"><span class="kpi-value">Week 2–4</span><span class="kpi-label">First Discord rare-pattern documentation</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat error"><span class="kpi-value">Day 48–72</span><span class="kpi-label">eBay account listings appear</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat purple"><span class="kpi-value">€50</span><span class="kpi-label">Escalation trigger: eBay listing price</span></div>
</div>

The rare-pattern secondary market will emerge because the genetic system is deterministic — it will be reverse-engineered within 24–48 hours of soft launch — and Brazil as a Southern Hemisphere launch market provides immediate cross-hemispheric breeding access from day one, significantly accelerating the timeline.

### Three Postures

| Posture | Description | Assessment |
|---|---|---|
| **Embrace** | Official "lineage gallery" — anonymous showcase of rarest cross-regional patterns | <span class="rpt-badge success">Recommended primary</span> |
| **Fight** | Account bans for external trading | <span class="rpt-badge error">Not recommended</span> — unenforceable; generates backlash |
| **Ignore** | Accept secondary market as price of genuine scarcity (Neko Atsume model) | <span class="rpt-badge warning">Acceptable fallback</span> |

**Recommended path**: Build the lineage gallery for the Year 2 / Audience C content wave, giving the secondary market time to build community before official infrastructure arrives. Monitor eBay listing prices; if accounts list above €50, official embrace is overdue.

**Live ops risk**: Secondary markets create a two-tier player population — rare-pattern holders vs. others. In a game designed around anonymity and equality, visible secondary trading creates named players with publicised patterns and de facto social graphs organised around asset ownership. This directly contradicts the hard constraints on no-profiles and no-follower-graph. The live ops team must plan for this contradiction before it manifests.

<details class="rpt-collapsible"><summary>Secondary market metrics to monitor</summary>

- First rare pattern documentation date (Discord / Reddit)
- eBay listing price trajectory for "Between Ponds accounts"
- Fan wiki creation date and rare-pattern spreadsheet emergence
- Cross-hemispheric breeding coordination discussion volume
- Time from first Discord screenshot to first eBay listing

</details>

# Core Loop Analysis

Between Ponds' core loop — compose a haiku, attach it to a koi, release the koi to a stranger, receive koi from strangers, curate the Memory Wall — is architecturally sound at the macro level but contains a cascade vulnerability at tier two, a cold-start problem at tier one, and an unresolved dark-pattern question at the seasonal layer. All three must be addressed before production.

## Four-Tier Temporal Structure

| Tier | Duration | Actions | Retention Role |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Daily** | 30–90 seconds | Feed fish, check for visiting koi | Habit anchor |
| **3-Day** | 2–5 minutes | Compose haiku, release koi | Creative / expressive beat |
| **Weekly** | 5–15 minutes | Inspect arrivals, tend Memory Wall | Social / collection reward |
| **Seasonal** | ~3 months (real calendar) | Hibernate, breed rare patterns | Long-arc emotional texture |

This mirrors Animal Crossing's proven nesting structure. The architecture is sound; the vulnerabilities are in the execution of each tier's entry point.

---

## The Core Verb: Release Ritual

The game's primary action — tap-and-hold to lower a sealed scroll toward a rising koi — is a textbook contemplative UX **threshold moment**. Four embedded design decisions make it work: the scroll is sealed (eliminating post-release anxiety), the koi rises to meet it (making release feel consensual), the animation is unskippable (preserving emotional register), and the moment is private (no broadcast, no counter).

The ritual physically enacts the *kireji* (cutting word) — the form's deepest structural element. The 3-day cadence between releases implements *ma* (meaningful interval) as game pacing. This is not coincidental UX convenience; it is mechanically sophisticated encoding of the form's philosophy.

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>Playtester language — 'exhale,' 'offering,' 'prayer,' 'goodbye' — reflects the post-composition state. Notably, no playtester data exists for the during-composition experience. This is a critical research gap for the first-time user experience.</p><footer>UX Research · Evidence: Medium</footer></blockquote>

---

## Critical Vulnerability: The Haiku Composition Wall

The design places the highest creative friction — haiku composition — at **tier two (every 3 days)**. In nested loop theory, each loop level must deliver emotionally satisfying value at its own cadence or higher-frequency loops stop pulling players back.

**The Cold Pond Problem**: The daily loop (feed fish, check arrivals) has no intrinsic value if no koi are arriving. For new players, koi arrivals will be sparse for the first 7–14 days until outbound koi complete journeys and return. This creates the weakest experience precisely during the most critical retention window: **D1–D7**.

**Haiku Composition Failure Cascade**: If a player finds haiku composition stressful — a non-trivial cohort given creative anxiety and linguistic friction for non-syllabic-language speakers — the every-3-days creation loop collapses. When it collapses, the weekly breeding loop never pays off, and the seasonal rare-pattern loop never becomes visible. The loops are too tightly chained: failure at tier 2 cascades through tiers 3 and 4.

**FTUE specific risk mode**: A player composes a haiku they dislike, releases it (the gesture feels irreversible), and feels exposed rather than generous — the opposite of the intended "exhale." Between Ponds asks for a poem before emotional attachment to the world has formed. Animal Crossing, Stardew Valley, and Cozy Grove all spend 10–30 minutes giving players things before requesting creative input.

### Comparable Loop Analysis

| Game | Creation Requirement | Loop Redundancy | Cold Start Solution |
|---|---|---|---|
| Neko Atsume | Zero — fully passive | High | Pre-populated cats arrive immediately |
| Kind Words | Low — simple prose | N/A (no retention pressure) | N/A (Steam one-time purchase) |
| Sky: CotL | Medium — multiple parallel loops | High — redundant seasonal/daily/weekly | Synchronous other players visible immediately |

<span class="rpt-badge error">Critical Gap</span> Between Ponds lacks the loop redundancy Sky achieves through parallel progression paths.

**Recommended Fix**: **"Receive First, Send Later" onboarding** — pre-seed new player ponds with 3–5 curated "afar" scrolls from a community-curated pool on Day 1. This delivers the emotional payoff of receiving a stranger's haiku before the player has released anything themselves, inverts the expected order, and violates none of the eight hard constraints.

---

## Self-Determination Theory Evaluation

Between Ponds' core loop is evaluated across SDT's three basic psychological needs:

<div class="rpt-bars">
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Autonomy</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill success" style="width:88%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Strongly Supported</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Relatedness</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill success" style="width:80%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Innovatively Supported</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Competence</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill error" style="width:30%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Weakly Supported — Critical Vulnerability</span></div>
</div>

**Autonomy** is strongly supported: haiku composition, koi release choice, and pond customisation provide genuine decision-making authority. The absence of daily quests and battle passes removes extrinsic pressure that SDT research shows undermines intrinsic motivation.

**Relatedness** is innovatively supported: anonymous koi exchange creates "ambient relatedness" — community belonging without social comparison pressure. Research from Sky: CotL found "the more compelling the goal, the more likely players were to ignore each other." Between Ponds removes goals entirely, potentially amplifying prosocial connection.

**Competence is the critical vulnerability**: no skill development arc exists. The 17-syllable constraint is fixed and never becomes more rewarding as players improve. SDT research identifies competence as the most frequently discussed construct in 85% of SDT-guided game studies. **SDT prediction**: strong early engagement from autonomy and relatedness satisfaction, but attrition in the **3–9 month window** from competence stagnation.

The breeding/genetics system is the strongest candidate for a secondary progression layer with genuine player agency. It should be foregrounded as the primary progression driver, not treated as a peripheral system.

---

## Darker Mechanics Assessment

<div class="rpt-debate"><div class="rpt-debate-header"><span class="rpt-badge error">High Risk</span><span class="rpt-debate-title">Drift Away — Dark Pattern or Impermanence Design?</span></div><div class="rpt-debate-body">The 30-day inactivity trigger meets the core dark pattern definition: "implied threat of loss to drive return engagement." The 30-day threshold is the standard industry win-back window. The game-generated farewell haiku is the tell — if the mechanic were genuinely about impermanence philosophy, the player would compose the farewell themselves. The auto-generation serves one function: keeping the message delivery network populated for receiving strangers. Compounding issue: the Winter Hibernation trap. A player who rationally reduces engagement during the designed slow season and closes the app on day 29 — then loses a koi on day 31 — has been deceived by the game's own seasonal aesthetic.</div><div class="convergence-bar"><div class="convergence-fill" style="width:30%"></div></div></div>

<div class="rpt-debate"><div class="rpt-debate-header"><span class="rpt-badge success">Low Risk</span><span class="rpt-debate-title">Memorial Pond — The Defensible Darker Mechanic</span></div><div class="rpt-debate-body">180 days is genuine absence. Nothing decays. The dormant shrine remains visitable. The "wake the shrine" return path is low-friction. The art direction (03-dormant-shrine) achieves the correct dual-coded ambiguity — neither punishing nor forgetting. Both the live ops manager and UX researcher independently assessed this as the most defensible of the three mechanics.</div><div class="convergence-bar"><div class="convergence-fill" style="width:90%"></div></div></div>

<div class="rpt-debate"><div class="rpt-debate-header"><span class="rpt-badge warning">Unresolved Edge Case</span><span class="rpt-debate-title">The Last Koi — Best-Designed Safety Floor</span></div><div class="rpt-debate-body">The refusal to allow a player to empty their pond prevents a specific catastrophic end-state — a player in distress systematically sending all their koi away as digital self-erasure — without requiring explanation, flagging, or punishment. Critical unresolved interaction: if Drift Away reduces a pond to one koi, does it respect The Last Koi rule? If not, a player could return to an empty pond — a severe emotional harm event the GDD does not address.</div><div class="convergence-bar"><div class="convergence-fill" style="width:65%"></div></div></div>

| Mechanic | Classification | Verdict | Risk Level |
|---|---|---|---|
| Drift Away (30-day) | Loss-aversion dark pattern with impermanence framing | Retain with modifications: Day 20 in-app warning; player-authored farewell haiku | <span class="rpt-badge error">HIGH</span> |
| Memorial Pond (180-day) | Sunset UX with emotional resonance | Retain as designed | <span class="rpt-badge success">LOW</span> |
| The Last Koi | Safety floor / harm reduction UX | Retain; resolve Drift Away interaction edge case | <span class="rpt-badge warning">LOW — unresolved edge case</span> |

---

## Genetic Breeding System

Between Ponds implements a genetic algorithm with three classic components: genotype (pattern-encoding state), crossover operator (blending two parent patterns), and mutation operator (small stochastic variation). The geographic fitness pressure — hemisphere-crossing rare patterns — is the game's most innovative mechanic and its most certain secondary market formation vector.

**The 40-Pattern Ceiling**: With 40 base families as vectors in pattern space, engaged players explore ~5–15% of pattern space in year 1, then plateau as their gene pool converges. The genetic novelty ceiling will be reached by engaged players within **18–24 months**. When the Memory Wall fills with familiar patterns, the primary emotional reward of breeding disappears.

<span class="rpt-badge warning">Critical distinction</span> Cosmetic-layer pattern additions do not expand the genetic novelty space unless introduced as *breedable* base families. A cosmetic skin that cannot be passed down genetically is a dead-end in the breeding system.

**Recommended commitment**: 4–6 new breedable pattern families per year, each requiring a specific breeding precondition to unlock and carrying documented cultural origin with Kyoto Koto Foundation sign-off.

The deterministic genetic structure will be reverse-engineered within **24–48 hours of soft launch**. Recommendation: publish the full breeding rule set openly at launch. Transparency converts a spoilable mechanic into a community-building one.

---

## Memory Wall as Phylogenetic Progression

The Memory Wall is not a collection mechanic — it is a **phylogenetic record** of incoming genetic contributions from external populations, pinned geographically. Each scroll represents an event in the player's pond's evolutionary history. This is a genuinely novel progression design: most breeding games track *what you have* (current population quality); Between Ponds tracks *where your genetics came from* (historical provenance).

Design opportunity: the Memory Wall could visually encode genetic influence directly in the koi swimming in the player's pond. A pond whose genetics derive heavily from Japanese senders might show more asagi and showa patterns; a pond with strong Southern Hemisphere influence might show the rare moonlight lacquer lineage. The wall and the pond would then be in visual dialogue, making genetic ancestry legible without requiring players to hold numerical data in memory.

---

## Engineering Architecture Gaps

Between Ponds is architecturally a **store-and-forward message broker**, not a real-time game. The routing service is the single most complex component: it must simultaneously satisfy breeding compatibility, hemispheric season balance, under-13 pool segregation, city-level location attachment without coordinate leak, and GDPR erasure handling for in-transit messages.

<details class="rpt-collapsible"><summary>Five undocumented engineering requirements</summary>

1. **Routing algorithm embeds compliance assumptions**: Hemisphere-awareness, child-safety pool isolation, geographic opt-out handling, and anti-spam are implicit but unspecified.
2. **Mid-flight state invalidation**: At 200k messages/day, ~200k koi are in-flight at any moment. Each must resolve correctly if the destination player deletes their account, becomes Memorial Pond, or changes age category during transit.
3. **Audit log vs. "not predictable" conflict**: EU DSA requires audit logs of routing decisions. Randomness in routing selection is compatible with deterministic logging — but this requires an explicit architectural decision.
4. **Anti-abuse routing requires account-level data** the no-profiles constraint discourages. The tension between "no identity footprint" and "auditable safety system" requires explicit resolution before development.
5. **Hemisphere default for opted-out users**: If an opted-out Southern Hemisphere player receives Northern Hemisphere seasonal timing by default, they experience seasonal mechanics one cycle off. This is a founding database schema decision.

</details>

<span class="rpt-badge error">Critical edge case</span> **GDPR erasure during transit**: if a recipient deletes their account while a koi is in transit to them, the current design does not specify redirection behaviour. The koi must be rerouted to the "afar" pool, not delivered to deleted storage and silently lost.

---

## Cultural Partnership: The Core Loop Dependency

The core loop's dependence on haiku's emotional register — *wabi-sabi*, *ma*, seasonal sensitivity — makes the Kyoto Koto Foundation relationship the single most load-bearing cultural decision in the design. The current arrangement (veto rights on execution, 1% net revenue, annual audits) does **not** provide affirmative co-creative direction on the core loop's emotional register. The Foundation can reject execution choices it identifies as wrong; it cannot originate the calibration decisions that determine whether the haiku composition UX feels, to Japanese players, like the real thing.

**The specific test**: Have Japanese players with no prior exposure play the early prototype and describe the haiku composition experience in their own words. If they do not independently reach words like *ma* (間), *mono no aware*, or *seasonal awareness*, the creative calibration is off — and the Foundation relationship needs to move from advisory to co-creative on this specific component.

*See [Player Motivation Profile], [Compliance Matrix], [Risk Heatmap], [Live Service Roadmap], [Ethical Considerations], [Monetization Analysis], [Player Journey Map], [Recommendations], [UX Heuristic Report], and [Competitive Landscape] for interconnected findings.*

---

# Theoretical Framework

Between Ponds does not merely borrow Japanese aesthetic vocabulary — it structurally *enacts* several distinct traditions simultaneously. Understanding each framework is prerequisite to evaluating any finding about cultural authenticity, monetization coherence, or Japanese launch risk.

---

## Japanese Aesthetic Traditions as Operating System

### Mono no Aware (物の哀れ) — Pathos of Impermanence

Motoori Norinaga's 18th-century systematization of a Heian sensibility holds that beauty is inseparable from transience. Between Ponds encodes this as its core operating principle: koi released are gone, messages cannot be re-read, and Drift Away removes koi permanently. The asymmetry of the Memory Wall — you cannot re-read what you sent, only what you received — directly enacts the traditional insight that **the gift is owned by the recipient**. This is not metaphor; it is structural design.

### Kireji (切れ字) — The Cutting Word

The most important structural element of traditional haiku is the grammatical pivot that creates suspension between two images. The release ritual physically enacts *kireji*: the moment the scroll descends and the koi disappears is the cut. The sealed scroll — not re-readable after release — enacts the irreversibility *kireji* implies. This design choice, often framed as a UX constraint, is in fact a philosophically precise gesture.

### Ritual Art Traditions — Nagashi-bina / Ema / Tanzaku

Three distinct Shinto/Buddhist ritual traditions directly parallel the game's core mechanics:

| Tradition | Original Practice | Between Ponds Parallel |
|-----------|------------------|----------------------|
| **Nagashi-bina** | Paper vessels sent into flowing water to carry misfortune away | Koi release carrying the sealed scroll |
| **Ema** | Private wishes written publicly in sacred space | Memory Wall as visible-to-others personal archive |
| **Tanzaku** | Wish-poetry written on paper strips for Tanabata | Haiku composition as seasonal wish-making |

Japanese players will bring these ritual contexts to the game *unconsciously*. The cultural consultancy sign-off requirement is not bureaucratic caution — it is essential calibration for meanings that will be legible to Japanese players without explanation.

### Ma (間) — Negative Space as Interval

*Ma* is not merely negative space in the Western sense but meaningful pause that gives significance to what surrounds it. The game enacts *ma* correctly: overhead top-down composition, water as default visual, the 3-day message cadence. The interval accumulates emotional weight. The constraint is not freemium pacing — **it is the interval that makes the ritual meaningful**. Any pressure to accelerate the cadence in response to retention metrics would destroy this dimension.

### Wabi-sabi — Imperfect Beauty

*Wabi-sabi* celebrates imperfection, rusticity, and natural aging — creating direct tension with premium cosmetics that sell polish and idealized perfection. The Founder's Lantern, as a status marker of pristine golden glow, is an anti-*wabi* object. Premium items should trend toward patinated, irregular, handmade aesthetics to remain coherent with the game's philosophical register.

### Yugen (幽玄) — Profound Mystery

Profound, mysterious beauty that cannot be fully articulated. The Dormant Shrine frame's deliberate ambiguity is its direct enactment — and the reason that over-explaining the Memorial Pond mechanic in onboarding copy would undermine what makes it powerful.

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>The six aesthetic traditions are not decoration. They are the game's internal logic. A design decision that violates one of them will be felt as wrong by Japanese players even if they cannot articulate why.</p><footer>Cultural Authenticity Analysis · Confidence: 0.88</footer></blockquote>

---

## Historical Precedents for Impermanence Mechanics

The 'impermanence as mechanic' tradition in games is small but densely documented. Between Ponds draws on it selectively — and in one case, ventures past the documented frontier entirely.

### Core Theoretical Claims

**1. Impermanence that feels *true* produces meaning rather than frustration.** It mirrors the structure of reality. Players who experienced *Passage* (Jason Rohrer, 2007) described it as "the first time a game made me feel the weight of time." The mechanism was not loss-aversion — it was recognition.

**2. Permanent goodbyes within game fiction are not experienced as punishment.** Animal Crossing villager departures generated elaborate farewell rituals: goodbye parties, screenshot albums, handwritten farewell cards posted to gaming forums. The players were not angry — they were grieving, which is a different and more dignified emotional response.

**3. Games can productively engage with permanent loss without punishment framing.** *That Dragon, Cancer* (2016) demonstrated this in the most extreme possible case.

### Mechanic-to-Precedent Mapping

| Mechanic | Historical Parallel | Confidence of Transfer |
|----------|--------------------|-----------------------|
| Drift Away (koi leaves, farewell haiku) | Animal Crossing villager departures | **High** — structurally near-identical |
| Memorial Pond (dormant shrine) | *Shadow of the Colossus*, *Dark Souls* environmental ambiguity | **Medium** — different genre context |
| Last Koi (final koi cannot be sent) | No direct precedent in casual/cozy mobile | **Low** — uncharted territory |

### The Auto-Generated Farewell Haiku as Critical Design Choice

The departing koi's farewell haiku — game-authored, not player-authored — is the pivot point for the Animal Crossing analogy. In Animal Crossing, departure dialogue is generated by the game but attributed to the villager *as character*. In Between Ponds, the game writes a farewell in what reads as the **player's own voice**. This is the structural point where the analogy breaks, and where dark pattern critique gains purchase.

The mechanism of loss-aversion is present in both contexts. Universal regard for Animal Crossing's mechanic as emotionally sophisticated rather than manipulative suggests that **execution is the variable** — specifically whether the player feels the koi chose to leave rather than was taken as a penalty.

### The Last Koi — Unprecedented Design

<div class="rpt-kpi">
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat warning"><span class="kpi-value">0</span><span class="kpi-label">Historical Precedents</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat error"><span class="kpi-value">Low</span><span class="kpi-label">Evidence Confidence</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat accent"><span class="kpi-value">Uncharted</span><span class="kpi-label">Design Territory</span></div>
</div>

No casual/cozy mobile game has shipped a mechanic where the final content item leaves and the game ends rather than resetting. The roguelike permadeath tradition is too different in genre context to provide clean evidence. This is either profound design integrity or an onboarding catastrophe — historical evidence cannot adjudicate. Soft launch data from Portugal and New Zealand will be the first evidence available.

---

## Seasonal Mechanics and Mindfulness Design

### Winter Hibernation as Mindfulness Feature

Research on circadian and seasonal wellness supports products that respect natural rhythms rather than fighting them with artificial stimulation. Winter hibernation in a wellness product aligns with users' actual context rather than demanding consistent high engagement regardless of season. The lantern-as-presence-signal is elegant and non-coercive: it asks for minimal presence (not daily engagement, not streaks) rather than demanding performance. This is meaningfully different from Duolingo's owl.

**Critical design tension:** The 30-day inactivity window runs during winter. A light user who engages at the game's own documented lowest frequency during the season the game itself signals reduced activity will lose a koi on Day 30. **The game induces reduced engagement by design, then penalizes that behavior** — a compound that may constitute an unfair commercial practice under EU Directive 2005/29/EC.

> **Recommended fix:** Pause or extend the Drift Away counter during Winter Hibernation. Koi cannot leave in winter — they are hibernating.

### Winter Hibernation as Narrative Framework

Playtesters described winter as "the best reason to come back in spring" and "the part where I missed my pond the most" — remarkable responses for a feature that *reduces* engagement. But these are retained players, not new winter installs. The cold-start failure mode — players who install during November–January and immediately encounter a 3-month low-activity state — remains entirely unmodeled.

### The Southern Hemisphere Narrative Problem

The hemispheric inversion is a narrative coherence problem, not merely a UX inconsistency. Between Ponds' entire aesthetic vocabulary — winter hibernation, spring breeding, cherry blossoms — is coded in Northern Hemisphere literary tradition. A Brazilian player launching in autumn 2027 is sold "quiet morning pond with cherry blossoms" but opens the game to find ice and sleeping fish.

<div class="rpt-bars">
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Northern Hemisphere narrative coherence</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill success" style="width:90%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">90%</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Southern Hemisphere (Brazil) narrative coherence</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill error" style="width:25%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">25%</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Equatorial dry-season specification completeness</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:15%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">15%</span></div>
</div>

The "dry season" equivalent for equatorial players is noted but unspecified with any narrative richness. The art/02 winter frame has no dry-season counterpart — no emotional image equivalent for a São Paulo player in July. **Recommended:** Commission a Southern Hemisphere equivalent of the art/02 frame — not a reskin, but a distinct image coded to that region's seasonal rest concept. Brazil's emotional equivalent of "the pond at rest" might be dry stone, low water, listless heat.

---

## Gift Economy as Analytical Lens

Marcel Mauss's *The Gift* (1925) provides the most coherent analytical framework for understanding Between Ponds' social mechanics as a whole.

### The Maussian Framework Applied

Mauss identifies three obligations in gift exchange: to give, to receive, and to reciprocate. Between Ponds deliberately breaks the third obligation — reciprocation is permitted but not required, not tracked, and not rewarded by the progression system.

**The Maussian bargain:** Fourcade & Kluttz (2020) name the design pattern — "aestheticizing gift-giving while embedding the pleasure of accumulation." Between Ponds aestheticizes the act of *sending* (the release ritual, the ceremony of the sealed scroll) while structurally rewarding the act of *receiving* (the Memory Wall, the world map pins, the progression architecture).

### Three Emergent Behaviors the Maussian Lens Predicts

**1. Social stratification without profiles.** Even without usernames, players will develop an implicit status hierarchy based on Memory Wall density. Players with the most incoming messages are the most socially "wealthy" in the game's implicit economy.

**2. Gift deflation over time.** Repeated asymmetric exchange in a gift economy eventually creates structural resentment. Players who consistently give without receiving will accumulate evidence of deselection. At scale, this produces churn that looks like retention failure but is actually social-rejection exit.

**3. The reciprocation mechanic as escape valve.** The koi return mechanic — sending a koi back to where a received koi originated — functions as an optional reciprocation mechanism. If players discover and use it widely, it partially restores the Maussian reciprocation obligation and may reduce giver-depletion. If players don't discover or use it, the asymmetry compounds.

### Cross-Domain Connections

| Connected Domain | Connection |
|-----------------|------------|
| Haiku pedagogy | The *renku* tradition is a gift exchange of verses — each participant both gives and receives |
| Player psychology | Therapeutic value of composing may partially compensate givers for low receipt rates |
| F2P economics | If 'receiver archetype' is the primary emotional beneficiary, monetization should target them (Memory Wall cosmetics) not the giver |

*The Vulnerability Registry details how these theoretical tensions manifest as specific exploitable risks.*

---

# Player Journey Map

The player journey in Between Ponds is not a single path but three incompatible paths arriving at the same door — each audience segment carrying a fundamentally different mental model of what the first session will deliver. Mapping those divergences is the prerequisite to any honest assessment of the "all three audiences, sequenced" positioning strategy.

---

## Audience Mental Model Conflicts at Onboarding

### Cozy Game Audience (Audience A)

**Pre-install expectation:** Immediate agency, something to do right now, visible rewards within five minutes, a clear picture of what the game looks like in three months.

**Session 1 experience:** Pond with three fish + request to write a poem + wait.

**Critical failure point:** The 8–36 hour delivery delay at the end of Session 1 is a structural mismatch with cozy pacing expectation. Cozy games characteristically reward accumulation and self-expression archives. The sealed scroll — players cannot re-read their own outgoing messages, cannot archive their creative output — is philosophically hostile to this audience. They expect to keep what they make.

<span class="rpt-badge error">INCOMPATIBLE</span> The sealed scroll cannot be reconciled with cozy game audience expectations. This is a values question, not a sequencing question.

### Mindfulness App Audience (Audience B)

**Pre-install expectation:** Calm, low-obligation interaction with immediate emotional payoff; comfortable with daily rituals; no performance pressure.

**Session 1 experience:** Creative performance pressure — 17 syllables, correctly counted, thematically appropriate, destined for a stranger's permanent Memory Wall.

**Critical comparison:** Kind Words' free-text letter format is qualitatively less constrained. Between Ponds is meaningfully *harder* to contribute to than the mindfulness app comparators. The haiku constraint's cognitive structure is philosophically aligned with mindfulness practice, but players arriving from Headspace or Finch are not expecting to demonstrate creative competence in their first five minutes.

<span class="rpt-badge warning">MEDIUM RISK</span> Strong philosophical fit with long-term retention; high composition anxiety risk at onboarding.

### Collectible-Social Art Audience (Audience C)

**Pre-install expectation:** Emergent social moments, visible rarity signals, collection that grows in aesthetic diversity.

**Session 1 experience:** Core collection mechanic (breeding) inaccessible in first sessions; 3-day composition cadence makes collection growth slow; rare patterns are seasonal — months away.

**Critical comparison:** Sky players walk the world in real time. Neko Atsume shows cat visits within hours. Between Ponds' breeding peaks are seasonal. The collection value is real but deferred by months.

<span class="rpt-badge warning">MEDIUM-HIGH RISK</span> Highest long-term fit; lowest short-term gratification delivery.

### The 'All Three, Sequenced' FTUE Problem

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>A store listing saying 'tend a koi pond, write haiku to strangers, breed rare patterns' is simultaneously an Animal Crossing pitch, a Headspace pitch, and a Neko Atsume pitch — and reads as none of them convincingly.</p><footer>Audience Segmentation Analysis · Confidence: 0.87</footer></blockquote>

**Recommended resolution:** The soft launch in Portugal and New Zealand should test which mental model new players *arrive with* using a 3-question 'what brought you here' screen. Run A/B FTUE sessions with (A) cozy-coded, (B) mindfulness-coded, (C) collectible-coded onboarding, and measure D7 retention per group. That data — not the founders' intuition — should define the single primary FTUE path.

---

## Journey Phase Map

### Phase 1: Install → Day 3 (Activation)

<div class="rpt-kpi">
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat error"><span class="kpi-value">CRITICAL</span><span class="kpi-label">Risk Level</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat warning"><span class="kpi-value">&lt;10%</span><span class="kpi-label">Est. D1 Retention (no mitigation)</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat accent"><span class="kpi-value">26%</span><span class="kpi-label">Industry D1 Median</span></div>
</div>

A new player releases their first koi into a thin network and may wait 24–72 hours for any delivery acknowledgment. With no pre-seeded "afar" scrolls and a network that may not yet have reached minimum viable density, the first session is structurally indistinguishable from a broken product. **The game must pre-seed Day 1 with curated afar scrolls.** New players' ponds should be entered into a priority receiving pool where established players' koi are preferentially routed.

The haiku composition is the activation wall. Estimated D3 composition completion rate among eligible DAU: 30–50%. The syllable counter and kigo suggestions help users who have already started writing; they do not solve the blank-page problem for users who haven't begun.

> **Recommended intervention:** A "seed release" practice session that sends the first haiku to a moderated safe harbor rather than a real stranger, allowing players to learn the gesture without social exposure stakes.

### Phase 2: Day 3–14 (Bonding)

The async loop begins working as network density builds. Players begin receiving haiku, populating the Memory Wall. The 8–36 hour delivery window transitions from anxiety to anticipation for players who have bonded with the mechanic. The critical gate: **players who receive zero messages in the first week are at maximum churn risk.**

Network density floor is a structural concern: the game's break-even DAU (~150k) may coincide with the minimum viable network density for the async mechanic to feel alive. If "break-even" and "product works" are the same DAU number, there is no safety margin.

### Phase 3: Day 14–30 (First Drift Away Window)

<div class="rpt-bars">
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Standard casual game D30 retention</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:30%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">0.85–3%</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Async social niche estimated D30</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill success" style="width:53%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">5–10%</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Winter install cohort estimated D30</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill error" style="width:20%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Unmodeled</span></div>
</div>

For Northern Hemisphere November–January installs, three demotivating events arrive in rapid succession at the D30 cliff: sparse network, approaching winter hibernation (fewer arrivals, breeding suspended), and the first Drift Away koi loss. This is an undesigned live ops accident concentrated at the exact moment industry data shows highest natural churn.

### Phase 4: Day 30+ (Retained Core)

Players who survive the D30 cliff enter the game's strongest emotional zone. The Memory Wall begins to function as a cartographic archive — scrolls pinned by city of origin across a hand-drawn world map. PostCrossing (800k+ active members, 60M+ postcards exchanged with no numeric progression) validates that "evidence strangers wrote to you" sustains decades of engagement at this audience segment.

The player's own voice is completely absent from their long-term record: the Memory Wall contains only received messages, not sent ones. This is philosophically coherent but means the player has no authorial identity in the archive. For Audience B (mindfulness), this is correct. For Audience A (cozy), it is alienating.

### Phase 5: Hibernation and Return

**Winter as designed pause vs. churn accelerator.** The game frames winter as a three-month intentional reduction. Live ops reality: players who install November–January never experience the cherry-blossom promise of the hero shot. Their first 90-day retention window overlaps with the low-activity state.

The "wake the shrine" return mechanic — dormant player returns, finds accumulated messages, moss clears over days — is the most powerful re-engagement moment in the game and is currently **undocumented as a designed UX flow.** This is the game's best win-back tool and it is not being treated as such.

---

## Win-Back Toolkit Audit

Between Ponds has deliberately handicapped its win-back toolkit more severely than any comparable mobile game. This is a consequence of the hard constraints, not a design oversight — but it must be recognized clearly.

**Unavailable win-back tools (due to hard constraints):**
- Paid retargeting (Constraint 3: no ads)
- Social re-engagement (Constraint 5: no follower graph)
- Personalized push copy (Constraint 2: no free-form text)
- Return incentive bonuses (Constraint 4: no pay-to-speed)

**Available win-back tools:**

| Tool | Current Status | Optimization Opportunity |
|------|---------------|--------------------------|
| Event-triggered push (koi arrival, seasonal transitions) | Documented | Strong — seasonal transitions are natural re-entry moments |
| Drift Away email notification | Single message, loss-framing | Reframe as seasonal love-letter invitation, not loss notification |
| Spring awakening notification | Undocumented | Should be designed as a full campaign, not a single push |
| "Wake the shrine" return UX | Undocumented | Highest-value win-back moment; needs full UX design |

The Drift Away email is the only documented out-of-app re-engagement mechanism, and it is framed as loss notification rather than invitation — a significant missed opportunity.

---

## Hemispheric Onboarding Asymmetry

### The Soft Launch Confound

The Portugal/New Zealand soft launch pairing creates a confounded first-impression experiment:

- **Portugal** (Northern autumn 2027): experiences autumn mechanics — reduced breeding, slower travel, quieter pond
- **New Zealand** (Southern hemisphere, autumn 2027 = Southern spring): experiences spring mechanics — high koi activity, breeding season, cherry-blossom-consistent gameplay

Same soft-launch period produces diametrically opposite first impressions. D7 and D30 retention data from this split will be nearly uninterpretable for the metrics that matter: breeding engagement rates, messaging volume, seasonal mechanic onboarding satisfaction.

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>The 'best reason to come back in spring' playtester finding describes retained players, not new installs during winter. These are two different populations with different data.</p><footer>Seasonal Mechanics Analysis · Confidence: 0.87</footer></blockquote>

### Brazil Launch Timing Risk

A Brazilian player downloading in October 2027 at Northern Hemisphere launch:
- Enters Southern Hemisphere spring (active season — positive first impression)
- Experiences first winter June 2028, only nine months in
- Encounters cross-hemisphere asymmetry immediately in community forums (Northern players post spring breeding content; Brazilian players in winter)

**Proposed resolution tests:**
1. Compare D90 retention between New Zealand cohort (entering winter) vs. Portugal cohort (entering summer) — primary decision input for Brazil launch timing
2. Test hemispheric "warm-water buffer" for Year 1 players: moderated winter less complete for new players only
3. Drift Away suspension during player's first winter season

---

## Psychological Architecture by Journey Stage

### Onboarding (D0–D3): Autonomy Activation

Self-Determination Theory identifies the first session as the highest-risk window. The haiku constraint functions as a cognitive-load sweet spot: long enough to require genuine effort, short enough to prevent perfectionism paralysis. The kigo tradition embedded in composition support mirrors a mindfulness grounding exercise.

**Critical gap:** The absence of any player character or avatar creates zero identity investment in the first five minutes. Mobile onboarding research consistently shows lower D1 retention when players make no identity investment in the first 90 seconds. The fix is within hard constraints: use the pond and first koi as identity anchors — naming the pond and meeting the first koi by name resolves the attachment deficit without requiring profiles or usernames.

### Early Retention (D7–D30): Competence Gap by Language Background

<div class="rpt-bars">
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Japanese/English players (haiku culturally familiar)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill success" style="width:85%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">High fit</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Turkish/Arabic/Brazilian Portuguese players (5-7-5 unnatural)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:45%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Two-tier experience</span></div>
</div>

Players in the free-verse accommodation tier receive a visibly different first-class experience. This damages self-worth in a way the design does not currently acknowledge or mitigate.

### Mid-Game (D30–D180): Awe Induction

The Memory Wall's cartographic archive is an awe-inducing object in the psychological sense. Awe (Keltner & Haidt, 2003) produces reduced self-focused cognition, increased sense of connection to humanity, and increased prosocial behavior. As a Memory Wall accumulates scrolls from Tokyo, São Paulo, Nairobi, and Oslo, it becomes viscerally vast — making concrete what social media metrics obscure.

**This is the correct answer to Q4 (audience positioning):** the game's deepest psychological mechanism is most aligned with Audience C (collectible-social art object). The positioning sequencing should start with C, not end with it.

### Long-Term (D180+): Awe Habituation Risk

The awe mechanism may front-load its psychological impact and habituate over time. The game has no documented mechanism for sustained novelty generation beyond seasonal content and rare pattern breeding. Whether accumulating digital cartography sustains awe responses over months is not established by existing research.

---

## The Dormant Shrine Journey (Exit Phase)

After 30 days of inactivity, Drift Away triggers. After 180 days, the pond becomes a Memorial Pond — visible to others as a visitable shrine. The Last Koi preserves the founding koi indefinitely. These mechanics create a three-stage exit journey: gradual departure, transition to memorial state, permanent archive.

**The key asymmetry:** The dormant player who caused the shrine state has no experience of it. Only senders who happen to arrive at the dormant pond encounter it. The player's exit is aestheticized for strangers without the player's knowledge or ongoing consent — a post-hoc identity capture problem addressed in detail in the Vulnerability Registry.

*The Vulnerability Registry catalogs specific exploitable risks emerging from these journey stage tensions.*

---

# Vulnerability Registry

Between Ponds carries a substantial vulnerability surface across legal, ethical, clinical, technical, and commercial domains. This registry consolidates all identified vulnerabilities from the advisory panel's multi-domain review. Severity ratings reflect consensus across domain findings; single-domain assessments are noted where they diverge. *Full jurisdictional analysis is in the Compliance Matrix; full technical analysis is in the Technology Evaluation.*

| V-13 | Free-verse fallback (40-char lines) lacks harassment-prevention properties of 5-7-5 form | Social Safety | <span class="rpt-badge accent">MEDIUM</span> | Unaddressed |
| V-14 | Kigo system hemisphere-naive — wrong seasonal suggestions for Southern Hemisphere players | Cultural/UX | <span class="rpt-badge accent">MEDIUM</span> | Unaddressed |
| V-15 | KKF lacks nishikigoi specialist expertise — general aesthetics org approving specialized breeding tradition | Cultural Authenticity | <span class="rpt-badge accent">MEDIUM</span> | Unaddressed |
| V-16 | No gift economy mechanic — missing social purchase trigger that drives Sky cosmetic revenue | Monetization | <span class="rpt-badge accent">MEDIUM</span> | Unaddressed |
| V-17 | Dormant player's pond displayed in degraded state without explicit consent to that specific presentation | Ethics/Consent | <span class="rpt-badge accent">MEDIUM</span> | Unaddressed |
| V-18 | VPN hemisphere attack surface — IP geolocation can be spoofed to trigger rare cross-hemisphere patterns | Technical | <span class="rpt-badge accent">MEDIUM</span> | Unaddressed |
| V-19 | Mandarin routing error — Mandarin is monosyllabic and should use 5-7-5 mode, not free-verse | Design/Technical | <span class="rpt-badge accent">MEDIUM</span> | Unaddressed |

---

## Deep Analysis: Priority Vulnerabilities

### V-01 / V-02: Regulatory Non-Compliance — Reporting and Child Safety

<span class="rpt-badge error">CRITICAL</span>

PEGI's "restricted communication" definition requires at least one of: blocking capabilities, reporting mechanisms, or filtering tools. Between Ponds has on-device filtering but **no blocking** (anonymous architecture makes this structurally impossible) and **no in-game reporting tool**. If PEGI evaluators require blocking/reporting, the anonymous architecture creates an unresolvable catch-22 requiring direct pre-submission dialogue with PEGI before June 2026.

Brazil's Digital ECA covers under-16 for data protection purposes, not under-13. The current compliance framing is scoped to the wrong age threshold for the Brazilian launch market.

---

### V-05: Drift Away — Multi-Domain Vulnerability Analysis

<span class="rpt-badge warning">HIGH</span> · Four independent domain findings converge on this single mechanic.

<details class="rpt-collapsible"><summary>Expand full multi-domain Drift Away analysis</summary>

**V1 (Philosophy): Vicarious Speech Act Without Consent**
Drift Away generates a farewell haiku attributed to the player and sends it to a stranger without the player's specific authorization for that utterance. Per Austin's speech act theory, this constitutes a vicarious illocutionary act — the game speaks *as the player* with farewell social force, to a recipient who cannot distinguish it from a genuine human expression. The three-way asymmetry of knowledge (player unaware, recipient deceived, game silent) is the ethical core of the problem. Confidence: 0.90.

**V2 (Legal — GDPR Art. 22): Automated Decision Without Documented Basis**
The automatic loss of a koi plus auto-generation and dispatch of a message in the user's name constitutes a significant automated decision under GDPR Article 22. Legal basis must be documented — consent at account creation with specific disclosure, or legitimate interest with balancing test. The post-facto email notification is not informed consent. Confidence: 0.86.

**V3 (Clinical Grief Therapy): Enforced Loss Without Consensual Grief Ritual**
In grief therapy, a ritual is distinguished from a compelled experience by the subject's choice to enter it. Drift Away removes that choice. The 30-day trigger selectively punishes users most likely to be in acute grief — the first 30–60 days post-loss is the highest-risk window for mobile app disengagement (Shear et al., 2011). The single-notification design has no escalation path, no return ritual, and no therapeutic buffer for players who return after a hospitalization to find their koi gone. Confidence: 0.88.

**V4 (Dark Pattern — Winter Interaction): Compound Unfair Commercial Practice**
The 30-day Drift Away timer continues running during Winter Hibernation. A player who rationally reduces engagement during the season the game itself signals as quieter will lose a koi on Day 30. The game induces reduced engagement by design, then penalizes that behavior. This may constitute an unfair commercial practice under EU Directive 2005/29/EC, Germany's EGDF 2025 guidance, and the incoming EU Digital Fairness Act (proposed 2026, in force ~2027). The impermanence argument collapses into manipulation when the product designs the behavior it then penalizes. Confidence: 0.88.

**UK OSA Additional Exposure:** The auto-generated farewell haiku is technically platform-generated content, not UGC. The UK Online Safety Act places platforms directly responsible for platform-generated content in ways that differ from UGC moderation duties. This is a qualitatively different legal category than the moderation duties Lanternwater has mapped for player messages.

**Required remediation (consensus across domains):**
- Extend Drift Away to 90 days minimum; pause clock during Winter Hibernation
- Replace game-authored farewell haiku with player's last real sent haiku (or remove entirely)
- Replace email notification with in-app push 7 days before trigger
- Offer opt-in version vs. mandatory — test whether opt-in Drift Away produces better reactivation than mandatory

</details>

---

### V-09: Seasonal Patterns as Soft Gacha

<span class="rpt-badge warning">HIGH</span>

If new pattern families only emerge during equinox windows, players absent during that window permanently miss content. This is functionally equivalent to time-limited seasonal events in live-service games — but presented as a philosophical design choice. Relevant for: (a) consumer protection disclosure in Germany, (b) rare pattern access asymmetry as an unequal service condition under Brazil LGPD.

Compounding issue: equatorial Brazilian populations (Manaus, Belém) are permanently incapable of contributing to hemisphere-crossing rare patterns, creating structural community resentment in one of four launch markets.

---

### V-11: Child Safety Delivery Log Absent

<span class="rpt-badge warning">HIGH</span>

UK OSA standard requires a documented, auditable log of all cross-user message deliveries with age verification metadata. The event taxonomy must include `sender_age_band` and `receiver_age_band` as required fields from day one. This is not a future enhancement — it is a pre-launch compliance requirement for the UK market.

---

## PEGI 2026 Interactive Risk Framework

| PEGI Trigger | Between Ponds Status | Classification |
|---|---|---|
| Loot boxes / gacha | None — excluded by hard constraint | <span class="rpt-badge success">CLEAR</span> |
| Time/quantity-limited offers | None planned | <span class="rpt-badge success">CLEAR</span> |
| NFTs / blockchain | None | <span class="rpt-badge success">CLEAR</span> |
| Penalizing missed logins | **Drift Away (30-day inactivity = permanent koi loss)** | <span class="rpt-badge warning">AMBER</span> |
| Unrestricted communication | On-device filtering present | <span class="rpt-badge accent">CONDITIONAL</span> |
| Reward-based login | Neutral | <span class="rpt-badge success">CLEAR</span> |

**Apple Rating System Mismatch:** Apple changed its rating categories in 2025 to 4+/9+/13+/16+/18+. The game's stated "PEGI 12 / IARC 12+" target does not map cleanly to Apple's current taxonomy. Expected outcome: **13+ on the App Store**, which excludes the game from Apple editorial featuring for children's content and may filter it from family sharing recommendations.

---

## Legal Dark Pattern Exposure by Jurisdiction

| ID | Type | Jurisdiction | Description | Current Status |
|----|------|-------------|-------------|----------------|
| V-DSA-01 | DSA Art. 25 dark pattern | EU | Drift Away = manipulation via inactivity-triggered asset loss | <span class="rpt-badge warning">Exposed</span> |
| V-UCPD-01 | EGDF 2025 | Germany | 'Time-pressure mechanics threatening asset loss' = EGDF dark pattern | <span class="rpt-badge error">Exposed</span> |
| V-DFA-01 | EU Digital Fairness Act | EU | Engagement-mechanic dark pattern prohibition (in force ~2027) | <span class="rpt-badge warning">Timing risk</span> |
| V-DSA-02 | DSA Art. 16 reporting | EU | No user-friendly illegal content reporting mechanism documented | <span class="rpt-badge warning">Gap</span> |

| V-OSA-02 | Ofcom age assurance | UK | On-device filter + parental gate does not satisfy 'highly effective' age assurance | <span class="rpt-badge error">Non-compliant</span> |

## Technical Vulnerability Detail

<details class="rpt-collapsible"><summary>Show 5 technical vulnerability details</summary>

| ID | Type | Description | Exploitability | Severity |
|----|------|-------------|----------------|----------|
| V-T01 | Client-side trust boundary | On-device moderation logic runs on user-controlled hardware; bypassed via jailbreak/root | Medium | High |
| V-T02 | API payload substitution | Client sends moderation-passed payload; attacker can intercept and substitute different payload | Medium | High |
| V-T03 | APK/IPA reverse engineering | Filter bypass techniques can be extracted and shared on Discord | Medium | Medium |
| V-T04 | Haiku steganography | Coordinated harassment in 17-syllable coded language — passes ML filter, recognizable to target | Low (requires coordination) | Medium |
| V-T05 | City-level location as targeting vector | Coordinated harassment can route hostile haiku to targets in specific cities | Medium | Medium |

</details>

---

## Ungoverned Secondary Market — Consensus Vulnerability

Three independent expert assessments converge on the same core vulnerability: the rare-pattern breeding economy will spawn an ungoverned secondary market. This is a **timeline question, not a probability question.**

<div class="rpt-bars">
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Weeks 1–4: Breeding genetics data-mined, fan wikis published</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill error" style="width:95%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Near-certain</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Months 2–3: First account-trading threads on Reddit</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill error" style="width:90%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Very likely</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Months 3–6: Account sales on secondary markets (eBay, PlayerAuctions)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:75%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Likely</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Months 6–18: Influencer demand spikes for rare patterns</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:65%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Probable</span></div>
</div>

**Historical precedents:** Pokémon GO account trading on eBay within 60 days of launch; Nookazon Animal Crossing marketplace within 4 weeks of New Horizons launch; CS:GO weapon skins secondary market at $400M+ annual volume within 2 years.

**Consensus recommendation:** Design embrace. Multiple experts independently recommend sanctioning the behavior — an official Lineage Registry, an in-game display board for rare patterns, and an official Discord with studio-maintained rarity guides. This captures community energy within the game's social graph without violating any hard constraint.

> The saving grace: moonlight lacquer cross is *reproducible*, not permanently unique. If lineage display is presented as a *story* ("I got this from Berlin and Tokyo") rather than a *stat*, secondary market incentive is partially deflated.

---

## Psychological and Ethical Vulnerability Summary

<details class="rpt-collapsible"><summary>Show 4 psychological/ethical vulnerability details</summary>

**VULN-001: Drift Away — Cognitive Accessibility Failure (HIGH)**
Affected populations: anxiety disorders, OCD, health anxiety, social anxiety; active grief (clinically normal 30–60 day disengagement); episodic mental health (bipolar, PTSD, SAD — episodes routinely exceed 30 days). The graduated severity is inverted: 30-day trigger causes permanent loss; 180-day trigger creates recoverable Memorial Pond. Minor inactivity is punished more permanently than major inactivity.

**VULN-002: Memorial Pond — Social Guilt Mechanism (MEDIUM)**
Unlike Tamagotchi-style self-contained pet death, Memorial Pond generates persistent social guilt — other players' koi continue visiting a pond the dormant player is not tending. The grief therapist frames this as grief ritual; the mindfulness designer frames it as dark pattern. Both assessments are simultaneously valid for different player populations.

**VULN-003: Wax Seal Return Visits — Parasocial Attachment Risk (LOW-MEDIUM)**
The wax seal is the only persistent identity marker in the game. For bereaved or isolated players, a recognizable seal may become a displaced attachment object. The no-profiles constraint is ultimately protective, but the longing generated before that limit is reached may not be benign.

**VULN-004: GDPR Dead Letter Office — Sender Disclosure Gap (MEDIUM)**
When a koi is delivered to a dormant (Memorial Pond) player, the sender does not know their message entered a dead letter state — read by no one who can reply. Gift economy requires gifts be capable of generating responses; sending to dormant ponds severs this without informing the sender.

</details>

---

## Analytics and Moderation Pipeline Vulnerabilities

| ID | Vulnerability | Severity | Domain |
|----|--------------|----------|--------|
| V-A01 | On-device filter analytically dark — no telemetry on dropped messages | HIGH | Analytics |
| V-A02 | Two-tier language quality signal (5-7-5 vs. free-verse reply rates untracked) | MEDIUM | Design/Analytics |
| V-A03 | Moderation cost not modeled — $18k–$55k/year absent from financial projections | HIGH | Financial |

| V-A08 | Rare pattern access asymmetry — Brazilian vs. German players receive unequal service at identical price | MEDIUM | Consumer Protection |
