| 30-day trigger during winter hibernation | <span class="rpt-badge error">High</span> | Dark pattern / design integrity | Suspend Drift Away clock during hibernation |
| 12+ players experiencing identity ventriloquism | <span class="rpt-badge error">High</span> | Child safety | Extend to 120+ days, add player agency |
| GDPR 'no delete' vs. right to erasure | <span class="rpt-badge error">High</span> | Privacy / legal | DPO assessment; anonymous artifact resolution |
| Dormant shrine without ongoing consent | <span class="rpt-badge warning">Medium</span> | Privacy / autonomy | Explicit consent architecture at onboarding |
| KKF as licensing not co-creation | <span class="rpt-badge warning">Medium</span> | Cultural justice | Independent Japanese assessment before launch |
| Memory Wall 'progress = being chosen' | <span class="rpt-badge warning">Medium</span> | Mental health equity | Track wellbeing correlation; add quiet-pond signal |
| Free-verse tier structural inequity | <span class="rpt-badge warning">Medium</span> | Equity | Playtest audit; KKF cultural equivalence assessment |
| No clinical scaffolding for grief mechanics | <span class="rpt-badge warning">Medium</span> | Harm reduction | Add discreet regional support resource in-app |

---

*The Contradiction Analysis module maps the specific expert disagreements embedded in this ethical assessment — particularly the fault lines over Drift Away, the haiku form, and the KKF arrangement.*


---

# Contradiction Analysis

The advisory panel does not agree. This module maps the fault lines — expert positions that are internally coherent, grounded in real evidence, and mutually incompatible. The contradictions documented here are not errors in the review process; they are the most valuable output of a multi-domain panel, surfacing the places where the founders must make a decision that no single domain can make for them.

---

## Contradiction 1: Drift Away — The Panel's Central Fault Line

This is the single most contested mechanic in the entire review. Four domain perspectives provide analyses that cannot be simultaneously correct at the same level of description.

<div class="rpt-debate"><div class="rpt-debate-header"><span class="rpt-badge error">Deep Disagreement</span><span class="rpt-debate-title">Drift Away — Dark Pattern vs. Grief Ritual vs. Philosophical Contradiction vs. Timing Error</span></div><div class="rpt-debate-body">

**Position 1 — Dark Pattern (Behavioral Economics, Conf: 0.88)**
Drift Away exploits three simultaneous cognitive biases: loss aversion, the endowment effect, and sunk cost. The mechanic converts inactivity into felt loss — the definition of a FOMO dark pattern. Regulatory exposure under Germany's DSA Art.25, UK CMA 2023 guidance, and Brazil's CDC Art.39 is documented. The aesthetic wrapper does not change the functional category.

**Position 2 — Authentic Grief Ritual (Zen Aesthetics, Conf: 0.85)**
In Zen Buddhist and Japanese aesthetic tradition, *mujo* (impermanence) is not merely accepted but celebrated as the condition of beauty. Drift Away enacts a transition — the koi departs to a stranger's pond, its journey continues elsewhere — structurally identical to Zen temple practices of leaving objects where they fall. In a game explicitly designed around impermanence as its animating philosophy, a mechanic that enacts impermanence is not cynical. It is the game making good on its promise.

**Position 3 — Philosophically Self-Contradicting (Philosophy, Conf: 0.87)**
The game invokes Buddhist/Japanese aesthetic frameworks while its commercial mechanics systematically resist impermanence: the Memory Wall accumulates forever; rare patterns are permanent status markers; the Last Koi can never be sent; 'nothing decays' during dormancy. Between Ponds uses the *aesthetic vocabulary* of impermanence while its *commercial mechanics* are archival and accumulative. Drift Away is, paradoxically, the one mechanic that is genuinely impermanent — and also the one that reads as a dark pattern.

**Position 4 — Correct Intent, Wrong Timing (Level Design, Conf: 0.88)**
Drift Away is the correct level design decision for an impermanence-philosophy game. But the 30-day trigger is incoherent with the seasonal design. A player who stops playing in November because winter makes the game feel slow, returns in February, and discovers a koi has left has done exactly what the seasonal design invited — and is punished for it.

</div><div class="convergence-bar"><div class="convergence-fill" style="width:65%"></div></div></div>

**The shared finding that cuts across all four positions:** Three of four domain experts (Zen aesthetics, level design, narrative design) independently identify the **auto-generated farewell haiku** as the specific problem within Drift Away. The mechanic's philosophical wound is not the departure of the koi but the machine-written message attributed to the player. Two scholars propose the same fix from different starting points: the departing koi carries silence — or a unique marking indicating it came from a pond that went quiet.

**Resolution tests:**
- Show the Drift Away notification to players who have never heard the philosophical rationale; measure emotional valence (loss-anxiety vs. acceptance)
- A/B test voluntary (player-initiated release) vs. involuntary (inactivity-triggered) departure
- Suspend Drift Away during winter hibernation and measure whether this changes the ethical characterisation

---

## Contradiction 2: Haiku Form — Safety Architecture vs. Linguistic Exclusion vs. Narrative Engine

<div class="rpt-debate"><div class="rpt-debate-header"><span class="rpt-badge warning">Structural Tension</span><span class="rpt-debate-title">The 5-7-5 Constraint — Three Incompatible Framings</span></div><div class="rpt-debate-body">

**Position 1 — Safety Architecture (Multiplayer Design)**
The 5-7-5 constraint is the most elegant anti-harassment architecture in mobile game design — structural, not moderation-dependent. Safety benefit is real and documented.

**Position 2 — Linguistic Exclusion (Anthropology / Linguistic Typology)**
The constraint creates two-tier expressive citizenship: syllabic-language players experience the full emotional architecture; non-syllabic language players (including Brazilian Portuguese) experience a character-count constraint with no cultural meaning. This is not a localisation problem — it is a structural equity problem.

**Position 3 — Narrative Engine (Narrative Design)**
The constraint is neither safety nor exclusion primarily — it is a narrative architecture. The interpretive gap and juxtaposition that make haiku emotionally resonant are destroyed by the free-verse fallback. The game claims to be a literary form; free-verse makes it a message app for 40% of the global mobile market.

</div><div class="convergence-bar"><div class="convergence-fill" style="width:45%"></div></div></div>

**Resolution test:** Paired receiver-response testing — show 5-7-5 haiku and equivalent 40-character messages to the same receivers. Measure emotional impact, reply willingness, and perceived sender effort. Separately, run Turkish and Japanese player sessions and ask both groups what they thought they were composing.

---

## Contradiction 3: Kigo System — Localisation Problem vs. Cultural Hegemony Actuator

| Position | Claim | Implication |
|----------|-------|-------------|
| Seasonal Mechanics Specialist | Kigo hemisphere problem is a technical/localisation issue — options exist to decouple suggestions from seasonal mechanics | Fix is an engineering task |
| Linguistic Typologist | Kigo are a 400-year literary tradition, not a format. Producing 'Brazilian summer kigo' is cultural invention requiring specific authority | Fix requires cultural co-authorship, not engineering |

If the kigo suggestion algorithm is hard-coded from a Japanese *saijiki* (seasonal almanac), it actively discourages non-Japanese players from writing their own seasonal experience — not by preventing them, but by offering only Japanese seasonal vocabulary as prompts.

**Resolution:** Establish explicit scope with KKF for whether their mandate extends to authorising new climate-zone kigo vocabularies. If not, decouple kigo from seasonal mechanics for non-Japanese markets until the authority question is resolved.

---

## Contradiction 4: Memory Wall — Innovative Progression vs. Commercially Inadequate

<div class="rpt-bars">
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Narrative / Philosophy: Meaningful and unprecedented</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill success" style="width:85%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Strong</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">D30+ Retained Players: Works as emotional progression</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill success" style="width:80%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Strong</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">D7 Onboarding: Fails without content density</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill error" style="width:25%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Weak</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Agency feedback: Measures receipt not effort</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:40%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Limited</span></div>
</div>

Both positions are simultaneously correct at different lifecycle stages. The disagreement is not philosophical — it is temporal. The game needs an **onboarding progression path that provides a sense of agency before the Memory Wall accumulates enough content to function as meaningful progression**. Without this, the Memory Wall is an empty room, not a growing archive, for the first critical weeks.

**Resolution test:** Compare Day 30 retention for players acquired through 'living archive' organic framing vs. players acquired through performance UA. The acquisition channel will predict which player expectation is being set.

---

## Contradiction 5: Four-Market Launch — Stress-Test Asset vs. Operational Recklessness

| Position | Claim | Source |
|----------|-------|--------|
| App Store Analyst | Geographic diversity from day one maximises the cross-cultural magic of the koi delivery network; heterogeneous data is more valuable | Strategic |
| Live Ops Manager | Four simultaneous markets with different regulatory frameworks, ARPU profiles, content cadences, and seasonal calendars is operationally reckless for a 6-person team | Operational |

**Resolution:** A staggered 4-week launch sequence satisfies both arguments. Germany + Japan first (cultural coherence + shared GDPR framework), then UK + Brazil. This preserves network diversity while dramatically reducing simultaneous operational strain.

---

## Contradiction 6: Cultural Co-Ownership — Sufficient Partnership vs. Structural Fig Leaf

<div class="rpt-debate"><div class="rpt-debate-header"><span class="rpt-badge warning">Unresolved</span><span class="rpt-debate-title">KKF Arrangement — Is Consultancy Enough for the Cultural Home Market?</span></div><div class="rpt-debate-body">

**Position A — Structurally Insufficient (Anthropology)**
Anthropological literature (Rogers 2006; Young 2010) distinguishes cross-cultural adoption (creative authority remains with originating culture) from cultural exploitation (creative authority held by appropriating culture, originators are consultants). Japanese aesthetic forms are signed off by KKF. Japanese commercial logic is not. The structural gap: who holds final authority when cultural framing and revenue projections conflict?

**Position B — Sufficient by Industry Standards (Zen Aesthetics / Brand Strategy)**
The arrangement is meaningfully better than comparable relationships. Ghost of Tsushima had no structural co-ownership and was acclaimed in Japan. The two Japanese core team members (Hana and Kenji) are the primary mitigation — the Foundation is supplementary.

**The crux:** The anthropological test is not team composition but *which team member has final authority*. A Japanese Creative Director whose commercial decisions can be overridden by a German Product Lead is a creative-lead-as-consultant arrangement — structurally similar to the Foundation's own position.

</div><div class="convergence-bar"><div class="convergence-fill" style="width:30%"></div></div></div>

**Additional finding:** KKF is the wrong geographic authority for nishikigoi culture. A Kyoto institution validating a Niigata tradition will not satisfy the Japanese koi hobbyist community — the most culturally informed early-adopter segment in the Japanese market. The two institutions cover different domains and should both be engaged.

**Resolution test:** Submit the KKF arrangement to a Japanese cultural journalist or academic for independent assessment. Specifically ask: *'Does the decision-making structure give the Japanese co-authors genuine creative authority or consultancy authority?'*

---

## Contradiction 7: Three-Audience Sequencing — Courageous or Failure to Decide

| Position | Claim | Depth of Problem |
|----------|-------|-----------------|
| Cozy Game Specialist | 'All three audiences, sequenced' has genre evolution precedent (Sky, Neko Atsume both migrated organically) | Fixable with a plan |
| Brand Strategist | The brand cannot hold both wellness and artistic-provocation frames in the same press launch cycle; first categorisation is sticky | Structural |
| Neko Atsume Analyst | The three audiences are not cleanly mappable to Between Ponds' actual genre identity (gift-economy correspondence game); 'sequencing' obscures a genre misclassification | Foundational |

**Resolution path:** Choose the primary visual/textual frame for the storefront and first press outreach (Audience C: collectible-social art object, per the art direction) while maintaining a secondary narrative frame (Audience B: mindfulness) for influencer and community contexts. **Resolution test:** Soft launch A/B on store listing copy.

---

## Contradiction 8: Secondary Market — Fight, Ignore, or Embrace

| Domain | Position |
|--------|---------|
| Gift Economy Scholar | Design embrace is the only stable outcome; lineage display and non-transferability framing are the tools |
| Corporate Lawyer | ToS prohibition is required regardless, for legal exposure management; the question is enforcement design, not whether to prohibit |
| Child Safety Specialist | Coordinated breeding requests constitute consensual location disclosure outside the game — a threat model the safety architecture was not designed for |

These positions are not mutually exclusive. The lawyer's ToS prohibition and the gift economy scholar's design embrace can coexist: prohibit account sales in ToS for legal protection; simultaneously make organic koi exchange so narratively satisfying that secondary markets are less appealing. Monitor eBay/Facebook Marketplace from soft-launch Week 1.

---

## Contradiction 9: Neko Atsume — Marketing Asset or Marketing Liability?

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>The comparison is a marketing liability because the emotional contract of Neko Atsume (passive receipt, low stakes, no vulnerability) is fundamentally different from Between Ponds (active composition, emotional investment, grief-adjacent mechanics). Marketing to Neko Atsume fans as if the games are comparable will set expectations the game cannot fulfill.</p><footer>Neko Atsume Analyst · Confidence: 0.82</footer></blockquote>

**Resolution test:** A/B copy testing with Neko Atsume fans — 'watching cats arrive' vs. 'sending poems to strangers.' If audience overlap is less than 40%, the comparison is a net liability.

---

## Contradiction 10: High Koi Attachment — Monetisation Feature vs. Monetisation Risk

| Position | Claim |
|----------|-------|
| Monetisation Designer (implied) | High attachment drives cosmetic spending — players who love their koi will pay to beautify their environment |
| Psychologist | High attachment + Drift Away loss creates post-loss hedonic dampening — players returning after losing a koi may experience spending guilt rather than spending motivation |

**The crux:** Drift Away should not simultaneously be the game's primary impermanence philosophy and a monetisation driver. If it suppresses spending rather than stimulating it, the monetisation model needs a trigger mechanism that does not depend on loss events.

---

## Contradiction Resolution Priority

<div class="rpt-bars">
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Drift Away auto-haiku (fix before launch)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill error" style="width:95%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Critical</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">KKF scope + nishikigoi authority (fix before launch)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill error" style="width:80%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Critical</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Three-audience sequencing (fix before marketing)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:70%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">High</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Memory Wall onboarding gap (fix before global launch)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:65%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">High</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Four-market stagger (operational decision, pre-launch)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill accent" style="width:55%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Medium</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Kigo localisation scope (design decision, pre-launch)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill accent" style="width:50%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Medium</span></div>

*The Knowledge Gaps module documents the specific empirical and technical information that would resolve many of these contradictions — and that the founders must either produce or acknowledge as blind spots before the round closes.*


---

# Knowledge Gaps

These are the questions the advisory panel could not answer — not because the analysis was insufficient, but because the information does not exist in the pitch materials. Every gap listed here represents a decision the founders either have not made, have not documented, or have not disclosed. Investors and regulators will ask about all of them.

---

## Gap Severity Overview

<div class="rpt-kpi">
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat error"><span class="kpi-value">5</span><span class="kpi-label">Critical Gaps</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat warning"><span class="kpi-value">9</span><span class="kpi-label">High Gaps</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat accent"><span class="kpi-value">8</span><span class="kpi-label">Medium Gaps</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat"><span class="kpi-value">22</span><span class="kpi-label">Total Identified</span></div>
</div>

---

## Critical Gaps — Must Close Before Round Presents

### GAP-C1: Auto-Generated Drift Away Haiku — Quality, Method, Consent <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

This is the single most load-bearing unresolved design question in the entire brief. The game bible states 'game-written farewell haiku' but does not specify:

- **Generation method:** Template bank? Procedural assembly? LLM? Curated human-written bank?
- **Quality bar:** What does a sample output look like?
- **Consent architecture:** At what point does the player consent to a machine-authored message being sent in their name to a stranger?
- **Disclosure plan:** Is the auto-generated nature disclosed to the receiving player?

The ethical, legal, narrative, and cultural character of the entire Drift Away mechanic pivots on this single unspecified detail. Multiple expert domains (philosophy, gift economy, narrative design, haiku pedagogy, legal) identified it independently. **No other gap has this many downstream implications.**

**What to do:** Produce sample outputs before the round presents. Specify the generation method in the GDD. Consult a German privacy lawyer on the *Urheberpersönlichkeitsrecht* (moral rights in authorship) exposure.

---

### GAP-C2: UK Online Safety Act — Children's Risk Assessment Not Documented <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

The UK Online Safety Act requires a formal Children's Risk Assessment before operating any service likely accessed by children. No mention of this assessment being planned appears in the pitch materials. Given the 2027 launch timeline there is time to complete it — but it must be documented and producible to Ofcom on request.

Additionally: CSAM detection capability is required under the OSA and is not mentioned anywhere in the safety stack description. The haiku form constraint reduces risk but does not eliminate the regulatory assessment requirement.

---

### GAP-C3: OSA Escalation Path and Reporting Mechanisms — Absent <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

The OSA requires documented escalation paths for safety incidents and user-facing mechanisms for reporting harmful content. The current design philosophy ('suspect messages are silently dropped') has no user-facing reporting mechanism and no documented human review escalation. This is not a design preference — it is a UK regulatory requirement that applies from day one of UK launch.

---

### GAP-C4: GDPR Deletion Cascade Architecture — Unresolved <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

When a sender requests account deletion under GDPR Art. 17, their haiku — now on a stranger's Memory Wall — may constitute personal data subject to erasure. The game's 'no delete' design philosophy for the Memory Wall conflicts with this legal obligation. The 'transform rather than delete' resolution (remove seal + city, preserve haiku as anonymous artifact) is architecturally plausible but requires a Data Protection Officer assessment of whether a transformed scroll satisfies GDPR Art. 4(1) anonymisation requirements.

**What to do:** Engage a DPO before the round closes. The anonymisation threshold question is a founding schema decision that cannot be retrofitted after launch.

---

### GAP-C5: Routing Algorithm — Unspecified for Compliance, Safety, and Social Quality <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

The game bible treats koi routing as 'magic.' The routing algorithm is the single most consequential unspecified technical parameter in the GDD. All of the following depend on it:

- Memory Wall progression quality (popularity-weighted vs. equitable routing)
- Compliance architecture (age pool separation for under-13 Calm Waters)
- Hemisphere detection (for rare pattern breeding)
- Dormant pond handling (active vs. dormant weighting)
- Network density modelling (minimum viable DAU for the social loop to feel alive)

**What to do:** Produce a routing algorithm whitepaper before development begins. This is not a later decision — it is a founding schema choice.

---

## High Priority Gaps — Must Close Before Launch

### GAP-H1: Under-13 'Calm Waters' Pool — No Design Document Exists <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

The Calm Waters pool is functionally a different product: curated haiku only, no user-generated content, no city location, isolated routing. Three regulatory frameworks impose specific obligations for this cohort: EU DSA, UK OSA, Brazil Digital ECA. No design document, UX specification, or content curation plan exists. **Who writes the curated haiku? How many? How are they approved? What routing logic applies?** None of these questions have answers in the pitch materials.

---

### GAP-H2: Winter Hibernation Cold-Start Retention — Unmodelled <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

The founders cite playtester data on 'best reason to come back in spring' — but this describes players who were already retained before winter. **No data exists on players who install during November–January and immediately encounter a 3-month low-activity state.**

This is the critical cold-start failure mode for a Q4 launch. Compounding factors:
- Drift Away timer fires after 30 days of inactivity — these players are at risk before establishing retention habits
- SAD prevalence in Germany and UK (1–6%) means some installs will coincide with the psychologically lowest-engagement period of the year
- Brazilian players installing in Northern Hemisphere winter begin in their spring — the seasonal narrative arc is inverted and unplanned

**The soft launch data gap:** Portugal/New Zealand soft launch in autumn 2027 will not generate winter retention data before the global launch decision is made. For winter data to inform the launch, soft launch must begin by May 2027 at the latest.

---

### GAP-H3: GDPR Right-to-Erasure Backend Architecture — Unverified <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

Whether the studio retains server-side records linking sender accounts to specific haiku is unspecified and unverifiable from the pitch materials. If the architecture truly severs this link at transmission, the GDPR right-to-erasure analysis changes materially. **No technical data flow audit has been possible.** A German DPA legal opinion is required before launch — this is not optional for a German-market launch.

---

### GAP-H4: Brazil Parental Consent Infrastructure — Engineering Problem Unscoped <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

Brazil's Digital ECA guardian-linkage requirement for under-16 users is a backend engineering problem, not a legal drafting problem. No technical specification exists in the pitch materials for age verification beyond self-declaration. Device-level OS API age signals (available on iOS and Android) are the least-friction option but their sufficiency for ANPD compliance is not formally confirmed.

---

### GAP-H5: Network Density Modelling — Break-Even May Equal Product-Works Threshold <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

The game's async social loop degrades below a critical player density threshold. The break-even DAU (~150k) may coincide with the minimum viable density for the mechanic to feel alive. 'Break-even' and 'product works' may be the same number — leaving no safety margin. **This threshold has not been modelled or tested.** If the game requires 150k DAU to sustain its core emotional loop, a soft launch at smaller scale may structurally fail to validate the premise.

---

### GAP-H6: Memory Wall Cold-Start — No Seeded Content Layer <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

At launch, with a small player base, koi travel time (8–36 hours) may return to a pool of other very new players with empty Memory Walls. The first social interactions will be sparse and low-quality. The game bible does not describe a seeded content layer — pre-written haiku from real authors that fill the network during the launch ramp. Without this, the first weeks of play feel like a waiting room, not a living world. **No beta cohort strategy or launch-partner programme is documented anywhere in the pitch materials.**

---

### GAP-H7: Compliance Cost Budget — Not Modelled in Seed Round <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

Year 1 compliance costs are estimated at €150k–€300k and are not accounted for in the pitch materials. The DPO requirement alone (€60k–€120k annually) becomes mandatory under GDPR Art. 37(1)(b) once the game reaches 600k DAU. This represents 8–17% of the seed round before a single line of game code is written. If not disclosed to investors as a material budget line, this may constitute a material omission in the raise.

---

### GAP-H8: Notification Architecture — Completely Unspecified <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

The GDD makes no mention of a push notification architecture. The 8–36 hour koi delivery window requires a notification strategy, but the game's 'no profiles, no behavioural tracking' design philosophy means notification timing cannot be personalised. **Without notification architecture, peak emotional arrival moments will be missed for a significant percentage of users.** The privacy-vs-relevance decision must be made and stated in the game bible before development.

---

### GAP-H9: Wake-the-Shrine UX — The Game's Most Powerful Re-engagement Moment Is Undesigned <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

The return mechanic for dormant players — clearing moss, lighting the lantern, opening accumulated scrolls — is the most powerful re-engagement moment in the game's entire architecture. It is currently not described as a designed UX flow. If 'wake the shrine' is implemented as 'tap yes to reactivate,' the studio has wasted its most powerful retention mechanic.

---

## Medium Priority Gaps — Resolve Before Development

<details class="rpt-collapsible"><summary>Show 9 medium-priority knowledge gaps</summary>

### GAP-M1: Kigo Dictionary Scope and Trigger Mechanism
The game bible mentions an 'on-device dictionary helps count syllables and suggest seasonal words (kigo)' but does not specify whether kigo suggestions are triggered by calendar date, in-game season state, player's hemisphere, or player's locale. If kigo are hard-coded from a Japanese *saijiki*, the system actively discourages non-Japanese players from writing their own seasonal experience. Scope must be defined per language/market.

### GAP-M2: Wax-Seal Data Schema — GDPR Reidentification Risk
Whether the wax-seal pattern is generated from non-personal parameters and cannot be linked back to any user record is unspecified. If truly unlinkable, the GDPR reidentification risk diminishes significantly. A German DPA legal opinion is required to confirm.

### GAP-M3: Drift Away + Last Koi Compounding Edge Case — Unmodelled
An inactive player progressively loses koi through Drift Away until reaching the Last Koi — which is then permanently protected but cannot be joined by new koi if no incoming koi arrive. The result is a perpetually dormant pond with one permanently stranded koi. **Required action:** Model this edge case explicitly; specify what happens to a Last Koi pond across a 12-month inactive timeline.

### GAP-M4: Drift Away Random Selection Mechanism — Unspecified
The game bible states koi are selected randomly for Drift Away but does not specify whether this is uniformly random or weighted (e.g., most-recently-arrived koi drift first, or common koi drift before rare ones). A weighting system would significantly reduce the 'punishes high-investment breeders' finding severity.

### GAP-M5: Moonlight Lacquer Lineage Mechanic — Ambiguous Specification
'A moonlight lacquer only appears when a koi whose lineage includes a Northern Hemisphere winter pond breeds with one from a Southern Hemisphere summer pond.' The phrase 'includes a Northern Hemisphere winter pond' is ambiguous: does the koi need to have been physically present, or does a parent's lineage qualify? If lineage-tracing qualifies, rarity dissolves at 12 months post-launch. **Required action:** Precise specification with example cases before development.

### GAP-M6: Opted-Out 'Afar' Players — Alternative Experience Unspecified
The game allows location opt-out to 'afar.' These players cannot participate in hemispheric rare-pattern breeding. In Germany (where opt-out rates may reach 30–50%), a significant portion of the first launch market is excluded from the most emotionally resonant breeding mechanics. **Required action:** Design and document the 'afar' player experience, including any alternative breeding mechanics.

### GAP-M7: Haiku Routing Table — Linguistic Assumptions Unverified
The brief implies Mandarin is routed to free-verse mode as a 'non-syllabic language,' but Mandarin is monosyllabic — every character is one syllable. A 5-7-5 haiku in Mandarin is exactly 17 characters. If the routing decision is based on an incorrect linguistic assumption, it should be corrected before development begins. **Required action:** Verify the routing decision table against actual linguistic structures for each language in scope.

### GAP-M8: Brazilian Portuguese Syllable-Counting Algorithm — Language-Variant-Specific Testing Required
Brazilian Portuguese has distinctive phonological features (nasal vowels, vowel reduction patterns) that differ from European Portuguese. A haiku counting tool designed for European Portuguese may miscalculate syllable counts for Brazilian speakers. This is a precondition for the Brazilian launch — not a post-launch patch.

### GAP-M9: Soft Launch Experimental Design — Not Specified
Multiple findings recommend A/B testing store listing positioning variants during the Portugal/New Zealand soft launch. No soft launch experimental design is specified in the pitch materials. Without pre-specified experimental arms, the three-audience positioning question and the Memory Wall cold-start question cannot be empirically resolved.

</details>

---

*The Accessibility Audit module documents the gaps that specifically affect disabled and language-minority players — a subset of the knowledge gaps above that require dedicated design attention rather than just documentation.*


---

# Accessibility Audit

Between Ponds has no accessibility specification in any current design document. The EU Accessibility Act came into force in June 2025 and is mandatory for mobile apps in the German launch market. The audit below consolidates findings across motor, sensory, cognitive, linguistic, and seasonal accessibility dimensions.

---

## Critical Findings Summary

<div class="rpt-kpi">
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat error"><span class="kpi-value">4</span><span class="kpi-label">Critical Failures</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat warning"><span class="kpi-value">2</span><span class="kpi-label">High Severity</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat accent"><span class="kpi-value">5–9 wks</span><span class="kpi-label">Est. Remediation</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat"><span class="kpi-value">June 2025</span><span class="kpi-label">EAA In Force</span></div>
</div>

---

## AUDIT-001 — Motor Accessibility: Release Ritual Gesture <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

The tap-and-hold release gesture is the game's **primary verb** — the only path through the core loop. It is a compound gesture requiring sustained fine motor control, precise sustained pressure, and temporal consistency.

**WCAG 2.5.1 (Level A)** requires that any function requiring a sustained gesture must have a single-tap alternative. No alternative is documented.

| Population | Prevalence | Impact |
|---|---|---|
| Essential tremor (adults 60+) | 4–7% | Cannot sustain reliable contact |
| Parkinson's disease | ~1% general | Hand tremor makes sustained contact unreliable |
| Switch access users | Variable | Cannot perform sustained contact via scanning interfaces |
| Eye-gaze users | Variable | No sustained contact available |
| Limited grip strength | Variable | Cannot maintain pressure for required duration |

**Severity amplification:** Unlike most games where inaccessible gestures block optional features, in Between Ponds the tap-and-hold *is the game*. A player who cannot reliably perform it cannot release messages, participate in the koi exchange, or progress on the Memory Wall. This is a funnel-level failure, not a feature-level failure.

**Regulatory exposure:**

| Jurisdiction | Law | Status |
|---|---|---|
| Germany | Barrierefreiheitsstärkungsgesetz (2025) | At risk |
| UK | Equality Act 2010 | At risk |
| EU | European Accessibility Act (June 2025) | Mandatory |

**Proposed solutions (all within hard constraints):**

1. **Long-press + alternative single-tap button in settings** — canonical fix; adds a settings screen
2. **Honor iOS/Android dwell-time settings** — set dwell time to 0 = immediate on single tap; zero implementation cost
3. **Procedural animation** *(recommended)* — animation plays to completion regardless of hold duration. Decouples gesture timing from animation timing. Preserves ceremony for all users; collapses to tap for accessibility users

---

## AUDIT-002 — Sensory (Vision): Memory Wall Spatial Interface <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

The Memory Wall is a spatial world-map interface with scrolls pinned at geographic origin points. No screen reader path is documented. Sight-loss populations in launch markets: UK 2M, Germany 1.2M, Brazil 6.5M.

**Recommended fix:** A list-view alternative — scrolls listed chronologically with haiku text and city-of-origin label — is both the accessibility fix and a general UX improvement. It serves sighted players who prefer scanning to spatial exploration.

---

## AUDIT-003 — Sensory (Color): Koi Pattern Differentiation <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

The koi pattern system relies on color as the **only** distinguishing dimension across 40 base pattern families. Red-green colorblindness (deuteranopia/protanopia) affects approximately 8% of male-chromosome holders — roughly 1 in 12 of the likely male player base.

| Mechanic | Failure Mode |
|---|---|
| Pond at Dawn (art/04) | Vermilion-and-white and pale-gold koi become near-indistinguishable under deuteranopia simulation |
| Memorial Pond (art/03) | Bright-gold Last Koi may lose contrast against muted dormant-pond palette |
| Collectible breeding meta | Cannot be meaningfully engaged if pattern families are not distinguishable — affects the primary Audience C retention driver |
| Memory Wall red wax seals (art/06) | Only sender-recognition mechanism; severely degraded contrast under protanopia/deuteranopia |
| Scroll text on aged parchment | Must meet WCAG 2.1 AA 4.5:1 contrast ratio; yellowed-paper aging effect may push contrast below threshold |

**Fixes within hard constraints:**

1. Add secondary pattern differentiation via scale texture and fin shape — more culturally authentic (Japanese koi grading uses skin texture as a major quality criterion) *and* more accessible
2. Offer a pattern-label toggle in accessibility settings (kohaku, ogon) — a UI label, not a messaging form; does not violate Hard Constraint 2
3. Specify minimum contrast ratios for scroll text in the visual design system before production art finalization

---

## AUDIT-004 — Linguistic Accessibility: Two-Tier Haiku System <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

The 5-7-5 syllabic form is native to Japanese and functions adequately in English and German. Turkish, Finnish, Arabic, and Mandarin speakers receive a free-verse fallback (3 lines, max 40 characters each). This creates a structurally unequal expressive experience.

| Population | Specific Barrier | Severity |
|---|---|---|
| Players with dyslexia | Phonological processing required for syllable counting; counter validates but does not enable generation | High |
| Players with ADHD | Sustained attention on constrained creative task; no draft persistence documented; 3-day cycle means failed compositions represent meaningful wait time | High |
| Players with expressive aphasia | Haiku form may feel liberating or frustrating depending on aphasia profile | Medium |
| Players with autism (literal language processing) | Kigo and poetic convention rely on metaphor and culturally-loaded imagery; valid haiku may feel tonally wrong, generating social anxiety | Medium |

**The under-13 model as accessibility precedent:** The GDD already specifies a fallback for under-13 players: pre-written haiku from a curated bank. This is exactly the accommodation that would also serve dyslexic and ADHD players. A **Reflection Mode** with 200+ human-curated haiku organized by season and emotional register:

- Does **not** violate Hard Constraint 2 (players select, not type free-form text)
- Does **not** violate the no-AI-generation rule if the bank is human-curated
- Preserves meaningful expressive choice (player curates self-presentation)

**Applicable standards:** Equality Act 2010 (UK); AGG (Germany) — indirect discrimination through language.

---

## Seasonal Accessibility

### Seasonal Mechanics and Disability Access

<span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span> The winter hibernation design and Drift Away interact to disproportionately harm disabled players.

| Issue | Affected Population | Severity | Proposed Mitigation |
|---|---|---|---|
| Winter hibernation as activity cliff for SAD players | ~1–6% Northern climate population; higher in Germany, UK | High | 'Slow seasons' accessibility setting (free, not monetized) |
| Drift Away firing during winter low-activity period | Players with chronic illness, housebound users, SAD-affected users | High | Suspend 30-day Drift Away clock during hibernation months |
| Content-thin winter coinciding with disabled players' peak play window | Disabled players with school/work-calendar constraints | Medium | 'Slow seasons' accessibility setting |
| Hemispheric asymmetry for Brazilian players | Southern hemisphere players installing during Northern autumn launch | Medium | Southern hemisphere-specific onboarding explaining seasonal arc |

*See [Compliance Matrix] and [Ethical Considerations] for legal dimensions of the Drift Away + winter + SAD pathway.*

---

## Full Audit Summary Table

| ID | Category | Mechanic | Severity | Compliant | Standard |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| AUDIT-001 | Cognitive | Drift Away | Critical | No | EU Accessibility Act + PEGI 2026 |
| AUDIT-002 | Sensory (Vision) | Memory Wall spatial map | Critical | No | EU Accessibility Act + WCAG 2.1 AA |
| AUDIT-003 | Motor | Release ritual tap-and-hold | High | No | WCAG 2.1 AA |
| AUDIT-004 | Linguistic | Two-tier haiku/free-verse system | High | Partial | Equality Act 2010; AGG |

---

## Priority Accessibility Investments by ROI

| Investment | Scope | Est. Time | Unlocks |
|---|---|---|---|
| Alternative tap-and-hold gesture (motor) | Engineering | 1–2 weeks | Entire motor-impaired population |
| Colorblind mode + texture differentiation for koi patterns (visual) | Art + Engineering | 2–4 weeks | ~8% of likely male user base from collectible meta |
| Memory Wall list-view + screen reader compatibility (visual/cognitive) | Engineering | 2–3 weeks | Blind/low-vision players + advocacy press coverage |

**Total estimated investment: 5–9 weeks combined, pre-ship.**

---

## Commercial Case for Accessibility-First

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>Games launching with strong accessibility receive disproportionate coverage from AbleGamers, Caniplaythat.com, and accessiblyapp — audiences that are highly motivated, word-of-mouth oriented, and underserved by mainstream gaming marketing. For a 6-person studio with limited marketing budget, this is non-purchasable organic acquisition.</p><footer>Accessibility Specialist · Confidence: 0.88</footer></blockquote>

The mindfulness app audience (Audience B) disproportionately includes players with anxiety, depression, chronic pain, and neurodivergent identification. Headspace's 2022 audience data showed 34% using the app for anxiety management. Finch's core retention driver is players with depression and social anxiety. **Designing for accessibility is designing for the core monetization audience.**

Sky: Children of the Light attracted a significant disability community through lenient input requirements, colorblind modes, and minimal fine-motor demands. Between Ponds' no-usernames, no-profiles ethos is already *more* accessible for social anxiety than Sky's social graph — closing the motor and visual gaps would position Between Ponds to capture the Sky accessibility community as an early adopter cohort.

The cozy genre has historically underperformed on accessibility. Animal Crossing: New Horizons launched in 2020 with no colorblind mode, no text scaling, no motor accessibility options. Between Ponds can leapfrog genre norms from day one at a fraction of the post-launch retrofit cost. The Last of Us Part II's accessibility features generated more gaming press than any single gameplay mechanic.

---

*The next section evaluates UX heuristic failures across the core loop — many accessibility gaps identified above are simultaneously Nielsen heuristic violations: see [UX Heuristic Report].*

---

# UX Heuristic Report

Between Ponds is evaluated against Nielsen's ten heuristics and standard mobile UX conventions. Findings span the Release Ritual, Memory Wall, haiku composition UI, Drift Away, and onboarding. Where heuristic failures intersect with regulatory exposure, compliance references are noted.

---

## Summary Scorecard

<div class="rpt-kpi">
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat error"><span class="kpi-value">4</span><span class="kpi-label">Critical Fails</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat warning"><span class="kpi-value">4</span><span class="kpi-label">High / Partial Fails</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat accent"><span class="kpi-value">1</span><span class="kpi-label">Unspecified (Critical Gap)</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat"><span class="kpi-value">4</span><span class="kpi-label">Regulatory Gaps</span></div>
</div>

---

## Heuristic Violations — Master Table

| Heuristic | Verdict | Issue | Severity | Location |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| H1: Visibility of System Status | **Fail** | Silent moderation failure at release ritual | Critical | Release Ritual |
| H1: Visibility of System Status | **Fail** | Empty Memory Wall as first progression view | Critical | Memory Wall |
| H1: Visibility of System Status | **Fail** | No feedback on why wall is sparse vs. dense | Medium | Memory Wall |
| H2: Match System / Real World | **Partial Fail** | Two-tier haiku creates second-class free-verse experience | High | Haiku composition |
| H2: Match System / Real World | **Partial Fail** | City-name rendering erases sender's linguistic identity | Medium | Memory Wall |
| H3: User Control and Freedom | **Fail** | No cancellation window for release gesture | High | Release Ritual |
| H3: User Control and Freedom | **Fail** | Drift Away has no recovery path; graduated severity inverted | Critical | Drift Away |
| H3: User Control and Freedom | **Fail** | No scroll deletion (GDPR Art. 17 conflict) | High | Memory Wall |
| H4: Error Prevention | **Fail** | Accidental tap-and-hold trigger — irreversible action | High | Release Ritual |
| H4: Error Prevention | **Fail** | Full Memory Wall display cap undefined | Medium | Memory Wall |
| H4: Consistency and Standards | **Fail** | No shop UI specified; no cosmetic discovery loop | High | Monetization |
| H4: Help / Recognize / Recover | **Fail** | GDPR erasure: scroll goes blank with no explanation | High | Memory Wall |
| H5: Aesthetic Design | **Medium** | Dormant Shrine ambiguity: neglect OR habitat — no context for visiting player | Medium | Dormant Shrine |
| H5: Accessibility | **Fail** | Memory Wall spatial map — no screen reader path (EU Accessibility Act) | Critical (legal) | Memory Wall |
| H6: Flexibility and Efficiency | **Fail** | Tap-and-hold conflicts with OS long-press; no accessible alternative | Critical | Release Ritual |
| H6: Flexibility and Efficiency | **Medium** | No routing preference signal for engagement mode | Medium | Koi routing |
| H6: Help / Recognition | **Unspecified** | Syllable counter implementation not specified | High | Haiku composition |

---

## Release Ritual: Detailed Findings

### H1 — Silent Moderation Failure <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

If the on-device filter holds a message after the player has completed the tap-and-hold ceremony, the player believes they released their koi. If the koi is silently dropped with no feedback, the player has completed a ceremony that accomplished nothing. This is a Nielsen Heuristic 1 violation at the game's most emotionally significant moment.

**Proposed resolution:** Explicit held-state feedback — a distinct visual treatment indicating the message is under review, separate from a successful release.

### H3 — No Cancellation Window <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

No cancellation window exists for the release gesture. Standard industry pattern (Gmail undo send, iOS shake to undo) not applied.

**Proposed resolution:** A 10-second post-release recall window — koi shown entering the mist, soft 'recall' gesture available. After 10 seconds, the recall disappears and the koi is truly gone. Preserves the permanence narrative while providing error recovery.

### H4 — Accidental Trigger / No Confirmation <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

Tap-and-hold can be accidentally triggered. Irreversible action with no confirmation step or cancel option means accidental triggers create negative experiences at the most emotionally important moment in the game.

### H6 — OS Conflict and Accessibility Barrier <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

On iOS and Android, tap-and-hold conflicts with system-level long-press behaviors (context menus, text selection, home screen jiggle). The game must intercept system events — fragile across OS versions — or provide a settings-level alternative. WCAG 2.5.1 requires any path-based gesture to have a single-pointer alternative.

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>The 4–8 second ceremony-to-message ratio may frustrate cozy-game players accustomed to faster tap-resolve loops in Stardew and Animal Crossing. The GDC 2020 Sky talk explicitly noted forced-pause mechanics lose players in 'efficiency mode.'</p><footer>UX Designer · Confidence: 0.84</footer></blockquote>

---

## Memory Wall: Detailed Findings

### H1 — Empty State as First Progression View <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

Before any messages are received, the Memory Wall is an empty room with a blank world map and no scrolls. This is the worst possible first impression for a system that *is* the progression system. Mobile UX research consistently identifies empty states as critical design moments.

**Recommended fix:** Seed with 1–2 'messages from the pond' (system-generated, clearly labeled as from the game, not strangers), or frame the blank map explicitly: *'Your map will fill as strangers write to you.'*

### H1 — No Feedback on Wall Density Drivers <span class="rpt-badge warning">Medium</span>

Players have no visibility into why their wall is sparse (poor routing luck? low release cadence? wrong hemisphere?) or dense. There is no feedback loop on what actions increase the probability of receiving scrolls — a violation of both visibility of system status and user control.

### H2 — City-Name Rendering and Cultural Identity <span class="rpt-badge warning">Medium</span>

The GDD states city names appear in the recipient's language, never the sender's. This is pragmatically correct for legibility, but creates a cultural flattening that works against the game's own stated purpose. City names carry etymology, colonial history, and self-identification.

The Memory Wall claims to be a cartography of received human connection, but the names on that cartography are all in the recipient's cognitive frame. Japanese cultural journalists examining the Memory Wall in the home market will have a legitimate observation about this. **The Kyoto Koto Foundation's sign-off should explicitly cover the city-name rendering policy.**

### H3 — No Scroll Deletion (GDPR Conflict) <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

The 'no delete' rule for received scrolls is philosophically intentional but creates a GDPR Article 17 compliance conflict. The 'release' option does not constitute erasure — the message continues to exist on another player's wall. Additionally, a haiku that is technically clean but personally devastating will pass the moderation filter and arrive on the Memory Wall permanently, with no recourse except re-releasing to another stranger.

**UX harm path:** this is not hypothetical. Upsetting content combined with no delete creates a specific failure mode that requires a reporting mechanism and a deletion path.

### H4 — GDPR Erasure Visual State <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

If a sender deletes their account (GDPR erasure), the haiku on the recipient's Memory Wall must change state. A scroll going blank with no explanation is a UX failure.

**Required:** a 'this message has been recalled by its author' state — a specific visual treatment (e.g., empty sealed scroll with a single character) that preserves Memory Wall spatial completeness while communicating unavailability.

### H4 — Full Memory Wall Display Cap Undefined <span class="rpt-badge warning">Medium</span>

What happens when the Memory Wall is 'full'? Hundreds of scrolls, densely packed world map. Display cap? Zoom? Scroll? Progressive fade? This must be specified before development. Similarly, the lanterns-illuminate-regions mechanic must specify a visual hierarchy for the high-density render state — 20+ lanterns at 600k DAU create a complex illumination pattern the brief does not address.

### H4 — No Report Button on Received Scrolls <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical (Legal)</span>

Under the UK Online Safety Act and EU Digital Services Act, services must provide easy-to-understand reporting paths for illegal or harmful content. An absent report button in the primary content consumption view is a regulatory gap, not a design choice.

**Required:** Tap to open scroll → report action must be present.

---

## Haiku Composition UI: Detailed Findings

### Syllable Counter Register Problem <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

A live numeric syllable counter (e.g., *'Line 1: 4/5 syllables'*) creates a graded, test-taking register that conflicts with the game's ceremonial emotional intent.

**Better design:** Show constraint as ambient state — a subtle fill-meter or tonal color shift as a line approaches completion. Make the player feel like they're writing a poem, not filling in a form. This is an unspecified critical decision with three radically different UX outcomes:

1. Static post-line display → grading feel
2. Live counter → flow-state but clinical
3. Live counter + diegetic scroll visual feedback → *exceptional*

### Two-Tier Form Divergence <span class="rpt-badge warning">High</span>

Syllabic-language players compose 5-7-5; free-verse players compose three lines, max 40 characters each. The brief does not describe what the composition UI looks like for free-verse players, or whether a Japanese player receiving a scroll from a Turkish player sees any signal that the message was written in free-verse mode. If not, the cognitive dissonance is jarring.

**Recommended solution:** Free-verse scrolls receive a subtly different visual treatment (different paper texture, different fold pattern) that communicates 'different vessel' without ranking one form above the other.

### Kigo Suggestion as Homogenization Risk

If 600,000 players draw from the same kigo list, the Memory Wall fills with similar vocabulary. Kigo suggestions should surface only after the player has written at least one line, surface multiple seasonal families, and include region-specific seasonal vocabulary for each launch market (sakura for Japan, Winterschlaf for Germany, dry-season vocabulary for Brazil).

---

## Drift Away: UX Analysis

### H3 — Inverted Graduated Severity <span class="rpt-badge error">Critical</span>

The game's graduated severity is inverted: 30-day absence = permanent loss; 180-day absence = recoverable shrine. The more severe consequence (permanent loss) has the shorter trigger window. This is a UX design error with dark pattern implications.

**Resolution:** Extend trigger; add multi-channel notification (in-app on next open + email); offer optional 'grief mode' accessibility setting (self-declared, no gatekeeping) that disables Drift Away and Memorial Pond mechanics.

---

## Onboarding: Identity Anchor Gap

### H7 — Zero Identity Investment in First Session <span class="rpt-badge warning">Medium</span>

The absence of a player character creates a zero-identity-investment first session. Within all eight hard constraints, the fix is available: use the pond name and first koi name as the player's identity anchor in onboarding. First koi named, pond named — these become self-representation without profiles, usernames, or follower graphs.

---

## Pay-to-Feel-Progress Risk

The cosmetic monetization model makes the Memory Wall display richer for paying players. Non-paying players experience their own progression less richly. This is not pay-to-speed, but it is pay-to-feel-progress.

**Test:** Usability session asking non-paying players at Month 3 to describe what they've accomplished without referencing lanterns. If they cannot articulate progress, legibility needs improvement for free players.

---

## Critical Regulatory Gaps Summary

| Gap | Severity | Regulation |
|---|---|---|
| No screen reader path for Memory Wall | Critical | EU Accessibility Act (June 2025) |
| No report button on received scrolls | Critical | UK OSA, EU DSA |
| No GDPR-erasure visual state for recalled scrolls | High | GDPR Art. 17 |
| Tap-and-hold without accessible alternative | Critical | WCAG 2.5.1, CVAA |

---

*The Remediation Roadmap in the next section translates these heuristic failures and regulatory gaps into a prioritized action sequence with timeline assignments: see [Remediation Roadmap].*

---

# Remediation Roadmap

This roadmap consolidates the panel's cross-domain findings into a sequenced action plan. Items are organized by urgency: before the round closes (next 30 days), before soft launch (Portugal/New Zealand), and before global launch. Each item is tagged with its source domain and a priority rating.

---

## Overview

<div class="rpt-bars">
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Before Round Closes</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill error" style="width:100%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">4 P0 items</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Before Soft Launch</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:100%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">8 P1 items</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Before UK Launch</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:75%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">4 P1 items</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Before Global Launch</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill success" style="width:50%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">4 P2 items</span></div>
</div>

---

## Phase 1: Before Round Closes — Next 30 Days

These items are investor-facing or create undisclosed legal exposure that must appear in due diligence materials.

### R1 — Resolve Auto-Generated Haiku Consent Architecture <span class="rpt-badge error">P0</span>

The game writes a farewell haiku and sends it in the player's name without explicit opt-in consent. This is the single most load-bearing unresolved design question in the current brief.

**Decision required:** Choose one of the following paths before the round closes:
- **Player-authored departure haiku** — in-app prompt at Day 20 inviting the player to compose their own farewell; no machine authorship
- **Curated poetic bank** — player selects from a human-curated farewell haiku set; preserves poetic frame without vicarious speech
- **Silent departure** — departing koi carries no message; philosophically coherent with mujo aesthetics

Eliminates the consent violation and removes the most defensible dark-pattern attack vector from the pitch.

*Sources: Live ops manager, Neko Atsume analyst, consumer law finding, Zen aesthetics finding, narrative design finding*

---

### R2 — Correct GDPR Age of Consent Gap for Germany <span class="rpt-badge error">P0</span>

Germany's GDPR Art. 8 consent age is **16**, not 13. The current PEGI 12+ design creates a non-compliant 13–15 age band in the home launch market. Raise the parental consent gate from 13 to 16 for Germany with documented parental verification. This must appear in investor due diligence materials.

*Source: Regulatory compliance expert*

---

### R3 — Commission a Data Protection Impact Assessment (DPIA) <span class="rpt-badge error">P0</span>

A DPIA cannot be completed internally. Engage qualified GDPR legal counsel to identify lawful basis for:

- City-level location data processing
- Memorial Pond dormant-state display (deceased player personal data)
- Koi lineage as a potential identifying data fingerprint
- GDPR erasure cascade through Memory Wall scrolls and koi lineage chains

*Sources: Regulatory compliance expert, corporate lawyer (two findings), community strategist*

---

### R4 — Run the PEGI 2026 Formal Questionnaire <span class="rpt-badge error">P0</span>

Do not assume PEGI 12 is achievable without formal assessment. The PEGI 2026 interactive risk framework questionnaire must be completed before the round closes. The result should appear in investor due diligence materials. The panel notes Drift Away (loss aversion mechanic with real-world inactivity trigger) and Memorial Pond (potential minor exposure to death-themed content) may push the rating above 12.

*Source: Genre benchmark analyst*

---

### R5 — Monetization Model Correction <span class="rpt-badge error">P0</span>

The current model understates platform costs and undershoots revenue potential simultaneously. Before presenting to investors:

- Add platform fee line (15–30% Apple/Google cut) to ARPDAU model
- Add audio cosmetics as a revenue category — unexplored, high-margin
- Add market-by-market ARPU modeling (Japan vs. Brazil differential is material)
- Clarify the implied €20M+ ARR target against the modeled €8.76M ARR (€0.04 ARPDAU × 600k DAU)

*Sources: Audio designer, F2P economist*

---

### R6 — Language Routing Audit (Mandarin) <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

Verify the Mandarin routing decision with the technical lead. Mandarin *is* a tonal language with a syllabic structure mappable to 5-7-5 (measured in characters/morae, not English-style syllables). If Mandarin is currently mapped to free-verse mode, correct to 5-7-5 with appropriate guidance.

*Source: Software engineer*

---

## Phase 2: Before Soft Launch (Portugal / New Zealand)

<details class="rpt-collapsible"><summary>Show 8 pre-soft-launch items</summary>

### R7 — Drift Away Seasonal Alignment <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

The 30-day inactivity trigger is incoherent with the winter hibernation design — players who reduce activity in winter (as the seasonal design explicitly invites) will trigger Drift Away. This is a design error, not a dark pattern. Options:

- **(a)** Suspend Drift Away during active winter hibernation (thematically coherent; simplest implementation)
- **(b)** Extend threshold to 90 days (one full seasonal window)
- **(c)** Count only 'active season days' (most accurate; most complex)

*Source: Level designer*

---

### R8 — Day 20 In-App Re-engagement Signal <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

Add an in-game aesthetic notification at Day 20 (not email, not alarm) that signals a koi is approaching departure. Reduces dark pattern criticism; improves re-engagement effectiveness; reduces the surprise-grief response for players who return after Day 30 to find their pond altered. This is the minimum viable re-engagement architecture.

*Source: Live ops manager*

---

### R9 — FTUE A/B Test — Practice Release vs. Full Stranger Delivery <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

Test FTUE sessions comparing Group A (full stranger delivery on first haiku) vs. Group B (seed release to a moderated safe harbor). Measure D1 retention and D7 self-reported comfort. The haiku composition wall is the most dangerous drop-off point in the game. This data is required before the final FTUE design is locked.

*Source: UX researcher*

---

### R10 — Hemispheric Onboarding Language <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

Add explicit hemispheric framing to onboarding: *'Your pond follows real seasons where you are.'* Surface this before the first session, not buried in settings. Prepare community FAQ and moderation script for 'why is my game different from theirs?' questions. The Brazil launch (Southern hemisphere) coincides with Northern hemisphere autumn in the current timeline.

*Source: Community strategist*

---

### R11 — Design Re-Engagement Email Sequences <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

The Drift Away email is the only documented out-of-app re-engagement mechanism. The win-back toolkit is severely constrained (no ads, no social graph, no return bonuses). Required: seasonal love-letter email sequences (spring arrival, equinox events, first koi arrival after absence) that function as re-engagement without violating any hard constraint.

*Source: Customer retention specialist*

---

### R12 — Winter First-Install Grace Period Design <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

Players who install November–January in the Northern hemisphere encounter a 3-month low-activity state before attachment has formed. Options:

- Accelerated onboarding for winter installs (richer first 60 days pre-winter)
- Reduced or delayed winter effect in Year 1
- Specific new-player winter content track

*Source: UI artist*

---

### R13 — Secondary Market ToS Policy <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

Publish a clear Terms of Service statement that accounts are non-transferable and the studio cannot assist with secondary market disputes. Must be in place before soft launch to be enforceable. The koi breeding collectible meta will attract secondary market interest.

*Source: Game designer*

---

### R14 — New Zealand vs. Portugal Retention Measurement Split <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

Establish D7, D30, D90 retention measurement split between New Zealand (Southern hemisphere winter) and Portugal (summer) soft-launch cohorts. This data is the primary decision input for Brazil launch timing and Winter Year 1 exemption design.

*Source: Retention specialist, UX researcher*

</details>

---

## Phase 3: Before UK Launch

<details class="rpt-collapsible"><summary>Show 4 UK-specific compliance items</summary>

### R15 — Complete UK OSA Children's Risk Assessment <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

Mandatory before UK launch. A formal Children's Risk Assessment identifying how the service could harm children must be documented and producible to Ofcom. The haiku constraint reduces risk but does not eliminate the assessment requirement.

---

### R16 — Implement CSAM Detection Capability <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

CSAM detection is a legal requirement under the UK Online Safety Act, not a best practice. The on-device filter is currently described as a profanity + PII filter. CSAM detection must be added to the safety stack before UK launch.

---

### R17 — Design User-Facing Reporting Mechanism and Escalation Path <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

The OSA requires: user-facing content reporting; human review escalation paths; law enforcement cooperation for serious harms. 'Silent dropping' of suspect messages is not a complete compliance framework. The design philosophy ('no punishment, just silence') must be reconciled with the legal obligation to escalate. A documented escalation architecture is required.

---

### R18 — Implement Robust Age Verification for UK <span class="rpt-badge warning">P1</span>

Self-declaration birthday entry almost certainly does not meet the OSA 'highly effective age assurance' standard. Ofcom guidance specifies: open banking, photo-ID matching, digital identity services, or facial age estimation. This is technically complex and operationally expensive — must be budgeted in the seed round scope.

</details>

---

## Phase 4: Before Global Launch

<details class="rpt-collapsible"><summary>Show 4 global launch items</summary>

### R19 — KKF Geographic Authority Expansion <span class="rpt-badge success">P2</span>

Engage a Niigata-based nishikigoi authority (Yamakoshi Village Cultural Heritage Organization or All Japan Nishikigoi Promotion Association) for koi pattern family review. The Kyoto Koto Foundation retains haiku and aesthetic authority; the nishikigoi authority covers koi-specific cultural content. This closes the geographic authority gap the panel identified.

*Sources: Art historian, anthropologist*

---

### R20 — Japanese Onboarding Copy — Gift Authorship Frame <span class="rpt-badge success">P2</span>

Write Japan-market-specific onboarding copy framing the haiku as the *noshi* — the 17 syllables are how the receiver knows someone chose to write for them specifically. Address the anonymous-hand cultural friction without changing the design. The anonymous gift is legible in Japanese gift culture; the handwriting recognition gap is what requires onboarding explanation.

*Source: Japanese cultural consultant*

---

### R21 — Commission Autumn and Winter Hero Compositions <span class="rpt-badge success">P2</span>

The spring/cherry blossom hero shot (art/05) cannot carry marketing materials for an autumn 2027 global launch season without seasonal mismatch. Commission autumn and winter hero compositions before global launch.

*Source: Creative director*

---

### R22 — Equatorial Player Decision <span class="rpt-badge success">P2</span>

Confirm whether equatorial player exclusion from hemisphere-crossing rare patterns is intentional design or an oversight. If intentional: write the community communication plan before players discover it. If oversight: revise the mechanic before launch.

*Source: Seasonal mechanics specialist*

</details>

---
