# Recommendations

## Overall Verdict

<div class="rpt-kpi">
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat accent"><span class="kpi-value">RAISE</span><span class="kpi-label">Round Verdict</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat warning"><span class="kpi-value">4</span><span class="kpi-label">Pre-Close Fixes</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat error"><span class="kpi-value">0</span><span class="kpi-label">Constraints to Remove</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat"><span class="kpi-value">C+B</span><span class="kpi-label">Primary Audiences</span></div>
</div>

The concept is fundable. Between Ponds has genuine assets rare in the indie mobile market: defensible differentiation (haiku constraint), a distinctive hero shot, cultural consultancy legitimacy, safety architecture ahead of regulation, and credentials that matter (Nintendo EPD pedigree, wellness product experience, EU trust and safety). None of the risks identified across the full panel review are fatal — they are design problems solvable with resources and iteration. **Raise the round. Fix these things first.**

---

## P0 — Must Fix Before Round Closes

### R1: Correct the Revenue Math

<span class="rpt-badge error">P0 · Finance</span>

The pitch materials contain a material omission: platform fees (30% Apple/Google standard, 15% small developer) are unaccounted for in the ARPDAU calculation. Effective ARPDAU is approximately **€0.023–0.028**, not €0.04. Break-even DAU is **250k–300k**, not 150k. ARR ambition at stated ARPDAU implies €20M+; realistic projection is approximately **€8.76M** (or ~€6.1M after platform fees).

**Required actions:**
- Add platform fee line to the financial model with scenario table (30% / 15%)
- Present per-market ARPDAU projections (Japan vs. Brazil differentials are significant)
- Add VAT treatment by market
- Add explicit compliance budget line: estimated **€150k–€300k Year 1** for four-market launch
- Reconsider the seed round milestone — '6 months of live ops' is insufficient; the game's emotional proposition matures at month 12–18. Either raise more (€2.5–3M) or explicitly state a Series A trigger.

*See [Supplementary Findings] for seasonal ARPDAU modelling guidance.*

---

### R2: Commission Legal Opinions Before Round Closes

<span class="rpt-badge error">P0 · Legal</span>

Four jurisdiction-specific legal questions must be answered before the round closes or shortly after — investors conducting due diligence will find these gaps:

| Market | Question | Urgency |
|--------|----------|---------|
| **Germany** | Does wax-seal reidentification (haiku + city + timestamp + lineage) constitute pseudonymization or processing of identifiable personal data under GDPR Art. 4(1)? | Before close |
| **UK** | Do hashed moderation decision logs satisfy OSA audit trail requirements? Begin Children's Access Assessment — **not after funding**. | Immediately |
| **Brazil** | Does koi 'release' satisfy LGPD Article 18 right to erasure? Clarify Digital ECA scope and geolocation parental control requirements. | Before Brazil launch |
| **All** | Commission a GDPR DPIA on message lifecycle before German launch — document server-side data retention, erasure propagation, Memorial Pond dormant-state lawful basis. | Before German launch |

Budget specialist counsel: UK digital law firm (£20–40k), Brazilian legal counsel, German DPA counsel.

---

### R3: Begin UK Children's Access Assessment Immediately

<span class="rpt-badge error">P0 · Regulatory</span>

The UK Online Safety Act is in force. A formal Children's Risk Assessment is required before launch — this is specialist work (not internal reading of the Act) and the timeline is long. Starting after funding closes is too late. Seek PEGI pre-submission guidance on whether the constrained async messaging system clears PEGI 12 communication thresholds, and whether on-device content filtering satisfies 'restricted communication' requirements or whether blocking/reporting functionality becomes mandatory.

**Critical failure mode:** If PEGI requires user-level blocking/reporting (not just content-format filtering), founders face a structural anonymity-vs-sub-18-rating choice. Know this failure mode before closing the round.

---

### R4: Clarify the Drift Away Notification Architecture

<span class="rpt-badge error">P0 · Design</span>

The pitch materials do not specify whether the notification fires **before** or **after** departure. This is not a detail — it is the difference between a grief ritual and a dark pattern:

- **Pre-departure warning + countdown** = punitive retention mechanic (DSA dark pattern risk, CMA 2023 guidance applies)
- **Post-departure notification** = impermanence design (philosophically coherent)

The design must default to post-departure notification. Never add a pre-departure countdown. Publish a design essay proactively framing the mechanic before launch to shape press narrative.

---

## P1 — High Priority (Before Feature Lock / Pre-Soft-Launch)

### R5: Cut or Mark the Auto-Generated Drift Away Haiku

<span class="rpt-badge warning">P1 · Design · Ethics</span>

Five independent expert domains (haiku pedagogy, philosophy, mindfulness design, clinical grief therapy, cozy game design) reached the same finding: the game-authored farewell haiku breaks the foundational promise that messages are human-authored. It constitutes a structural deception regardless of aesthetic intent and creates moral rights exposure in Germany.

**Panel-consensus resolution — choose one:**
1. Remove the auto-generated haiku entirely; the koi departure alone is expressive enough
2. Replace with the player's own last real sent haiku (highest fidelity option)
3. If retained: visually distinguish from player-composed messages (different scroll border, different seal design, explicit system attribution)

Additionally: suspend the Drift Away clock during the player's hemisphere's Winter Hibernation period. The 30-day timer fires on culturally predictable seasonal absences. Extend to 60–90 days or implement a seasonal grace window (December 15–January 15 and June 15–August 15). This is a thematic correction, not a philosophical change.

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>The winter hibernation clock-pause is additionally recommended as a consumer protection measure — not only as design coherence. A player who reduces activity during winter as the game's seasonal design invites should not trigger a punitive departure mechanic.</p><footer>Panel Consensus · Multiple Expert Domains</footer></blockquote>

---

### R6: Five Specific Japanese Launch Fixes

<span class="rpt-badge warning">P1 · Cultural</span>

| Priority | Fix | Timeline |
|----------|-----|----------|
| **CRITICAL** | Dormant Shrine visual review with Kyoto Koto Foundation — specific attention to torn scroll (ceremonial abandonment) and unlit lantern (mourning signal) which carry Shinto spiritual-warning readings that contradict intent | Before asset finalization |
| **HIGH** | Seasonally appropriate hero shot for Japanese App Store — winter hibernation frame (art/02 aesthetic) is the correct autumn launch alternative to cherry blossom | Before launch |
| **MEDIUM** | Japanese naming conventions for all 36 non-gosanke koi pattern families before feature lock | Before feature lock |
| **MEDIUM** | Do not present 5-7-5 as authentic Japanese haiku to Japanese players; acknowledge the Western haiku tradition distinction explicitly | Pre-launch materials |
| **MEDIUM** | For Japanese marketing: use Memory Wall pavilion (frame 06) as hero shot, not Release Ritual (frame 01); Japanese players are more moved by evidence of *what accumulates* than by the act of sending |  |

**Additional Japan-specific positions:**
- Do not use impermanence philosophy language (*mono no aware*, *wabi-sabi*) to describe Drift Away in Japanese marketing — reframe using *en* (縁, fate-connection threads)
- Position ex-Nintendo EPD designers (Hana Watanabe, Kenji Arakawa) as the primary cultural legitimacy signal in Japan, ahead of the Foundation relationship
- Commission Japan-native ASO strategy — do not translate the English store listing; position in 癒しゲーム (healing game) search category
- Clarify KKF mandate scope; add nishikigoi specialist (Zen Nippon Airinkai) for koi pattern review; a general Japanese aesthetics organization cannot credibly validate 40 koi pattern families

---

### R7: Add a Reporting Mechanism

<span class="rpt-badge warning">P1 · Compliance</span>

Add a single 'report this message' tap to the haiku reading view. This simultaneously resolves PEGI 2026 Safe Online Gameplay requirements, DSA Article 25 obligations, and UK OSA reporting infrastructure — without compromising the anonymity model or the aesthetic. This is the one recommended **addition** to the eight hard constraints; none of the existing constraints need to be removed.

---

### R8: Brazil Age-Verification and Under-13 Architecture

<span class="rpt-badge warning">P1 · Legal · Engineering</span>

Brazil's Digital ECA (in force March 2026) requires compliant age-verification for under-16. Engineering paths: device-level OS API age signals or guardian account linkage. This is a vendor budget item. Separately, the under-13 Calm Waters Pool requires its own design document — specify it as a separate product with adult-contributed curated haiku (opt-in contributor program), not studio-written messages, to preserve emotional authenticity within regulatory constraints.

---

## P1 — Design Gaps (Close Before Build Begins)

### R9: Solve the Cold-Pond Onboarding Problem

<span class="rpt-badge warning">P1 · Retention</span>

New players arrive to an empty pond. An empty Memory Wall with two scrolls on a vast map is psychologically deflating. Two complementary solutions that violate no hard constraints:

**Founding Pond mechanic:** Every new player's first 3 koi deliveries come from a curated pool of real player-written haiku (collected from beta) rather than the live network. Seeds the Memory Wall within the first week without fabricating content.

**'Receive first, send later' onboarding:** Pre-seed new player ponds with 3–5 curated 'afar' scrolls on Day 1. Instrument a 'first meaningful exchange' event — define and optimize time-to-first-meaningful-exchange as the primary early-game retention metric.

---

### R10: Design the Gifting Revenue Channel

<span class="rpt-badge warning">P1 · Monetization</span>

The current monetization model has no gifting revenue channel and no social discovery vector for cosmetic purchases. Sky: Children of the Light demonstrates this model at scale (22% of revenue from player-to-player gifting).

**'Send a Lantern' mechanic:** A cosmetic gift attached to a koi — anonymous, no usernames, fully consistent with all eight hard constraints. Players can purchase and send cosmetic lanterns as koi message attachments; recipient receives the lantern as a gift from a stranger. Creates gifting revenue, social cosmetic discovery, and organic word-of-mouth.

**Audio cosmetics as primary new IAP category:** Add instrument packs, ambient packs, composer collaborations, and pond-signature audio as a primary IAP category. The visual-only path produces ~€0.02 ARPDAU (Neko Atsume range); audio cosmetics are required to reach the €0.04 target.

---

### R11: Specify and Document the Koi Routing Algorithm

<span class="rpt-badge warning">P1 · Engineering</span>

The routing algorithm must be treated as a backend engineering specification before development begins — not a game-magic abstraction. Document: geographic matching logic, hemisphere detection, active/dormant player weighting, age-pool segregation for under-13, mid-flight state invalidation, and DSA-compliant audit logging (time, routing, delivery, moderation decision hash — preserves individual privacy while enabling network topology analysis). A 'weekend prototype' is not an architecture for 600k DAU.

---

## P2 — Strategic Decisions

### R12: Positioning — Choose One Primary Audience

<span class="rpt-badge">P2 · Strategy</span>

'All three audiences, sequenced' is not a strategy — it is a deferral. The panel's position:

<div class="rpt-bars">
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Audience C (Collectible-Social)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill success" style="width:88%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Primary</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Audience B (Mindfulness/Reflection)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill" style="width:70%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Secondary</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-bar"><span class="bar-label">Audience A (Cozy Game)</span><div class="bar-track"><div class="bar-fill warning" style="width:30%"></div></div><span class="bar-value">Do Not Lead</span></div>
</div>

The art direction already commits to Audience C. The sealed scroll mechanic is fundamentally incompatible with cozy game audience expectations (numeric progress, farming loop). Cozy players who install for those expectations will churn when they discover the absence of those mechanics. Audience A can be served through secondary messaging after initial traction is established.

**Market-specific variants** (not a unified brand voice across all four markets):
- **Germany + UK:** Lead with Audience C (collectible-social art object)
- **Japan:** Lead with 'a new form of letter exchange' (tegami/bunko frame — the analog correspondence revival community is the correct first-audience channel)
- **Brazil:** Lead with cozy social (mobile social gaming culture)

**Test:** Build Apple Custom Product Page (CPP) variants for all three audiences from day one. Run as paid UA tests during soft launch before committing to global metadata. Data, not intuition, should dictate final framing.

---

### R13: Launch Sequencing

<span class="rpt-badge">P2 · Operations</span>

Stage the launch rather than launching all four markets simultaneously. A 6-person team cannot operationally manage four simultaneous regulatory frameworks:

1. **Germany + Japan first** — cultural coherence, GDPR shared framework, maximum press impact
2. **UK + Brazil 4 weeks later** — after initial stability is confirmed

Add 2 hires (data analyst + live ops content manager) within first 6 months of soft launch, or contract a live ops platform.

**Soft launch setup:** Portugal (Northern Hemisphere) + New Zealand (Southern Hemisphere) is the correct experimental pairing. Begin soft launch **no later than May 2027** to gather Northern Hemisphere winter data before a global launch decision. Begin soft launch by May 2027 — soft-launch must begin by spring 2027 to capture winter data from Portuguese testers by December 2027. Soft launch without winter data = global launch commitment based on high-engagement season data only.

---

### R14: Develop the Darker Mechanics Within Clear Specifications

<span class="rpt-badge">P2 · Design</span>

| Mechanic | Verdict | Condition |
|----------|---------|-----------|
| **Drift Away** | Redesign — not cut, not keep as-is | Post-departure notification only; never pre-departure countdown; farewell haiku redesigned or removed; clock paused during Winter Hibernation |
| **Memorial Pond** | Keep and strengthen | Add opt-in 'hibernate' mode for affirmative consent to shrine state; diegetic signal for visiting players; GDPR lawful basis documented |
| **The Last Koi** | Keep as safety floor | Frame explicitly as *kireji* in marketing; expand GDD for 1+ year solo-koi scenario; specify pond-closing ceremony pathway for players who want to end with agency |

**PR sequencing for darker mechanics:** (1) Publish 'The Last Koi' design essay first — establish studio as wellbeing-thoughtful; (2) Publish Memorial Pond digital impermanence explainer second; (3) Let Drift Away emerge organically; respond via prepared statement referencing the already-published framework.

---

## P3 — Year 1 Live Ops and Post-Launch

<details class="rpt-collapsible"><summary>Show 8 Year 1 and post-launch recommendations</summary>

**R15: Seasonal Cosmetics Calendar — Brazil-Specific Track**
Brazil's seasons are inverted from the three Northern Hemisphere markets. The four seasonal pond themes produced on a Northern Hemisphere calendar will be systematically purchased by Brazilian players out of season. Options: (a) hemisphere-appropriate variants, (b) allow Brazilian players to unlock themes out of calendar order, or (c) reframe as thematic rather than calendar-matched. Model ARPDAU separately by season before finalizing financial projections — the winter trough ARPDAU may reveal a structural financial problem the annual average obscures.

**R16: Japan Golden Week and Shōgatsu Within Hard Constraints**
Design a Golden Week rare pattern emergence window (specific cross producing a pattern only during April 29–May 5). Design a Shōgatsu (Japanese New Year) visual state for dormant ponds — pine branches (kadomatsu), specific lantern color, crane in snow — that makes hibernation feel ceremonially Japanese. Both require KKF sign-off (constraint #6) but no gameplay mechanics changes.

**R17: Secondary Market — Embrace, Don't Fight**
The rare-pattern secondary market will form during soft launch. Monitor eBay and Discord from soft-launch week 1. If prices exceed €50, accelerate the 'lineage scroll' view (see *Supplementary Findings*) and the 'Migration Season' feature: twice per year, cross-hemisphere koi available for adoption (not purchase) through the existing release-and-receive mechanic. Preserves gift-economy philosophy and keeps behavior observable in-game.

**R18: Annual Content Roadmap — New Breedable Pattern Families**
Commit to 4–6 new breedable pattern families per year. This converts the genetic system from a fixed 40-family combinatorial space into a living content roadmap. Each new family requires KKF sign-off and a breeding precondition unlock.

**R19: Editorial Featuring as Primary Discovery Pathway**
Apply for Google Play Indie Games Accelerator 2026 cohort. Build Apple Developer Relations relationship early. Editorial featuring is the only cost-effective discovery pathway given zero UA budget.

**R20: Release Ritual Gesture Accessibility**
The tap-and-hold release ritual gesture creates a motor accessibility problem (EU Accessibility Act — mandatory for German launch). Resolution: adapt to a toggle or double-tap ('ceremonial mode') without making the ritual itself optional. The emotional experience is preserved; the physical input is made accessible. Motor accessibility alternative, colorblind + texture koi differentiation, and screen-reader-compatible Memory Wall list view represent 5–9 weeks of work with high organic UA return.

**R21: Expand Cultural Consultancy to Audio**
Constraint 6 (KKF sign-off on all Japanese-origin assets) must be extended explicitly to audio. Budget €15–25k for a Kyoto-based audio consultant with documented musical lineage. Per-asset review required for: shakuhachi recordings (provenance chain — Kontakt libraries insufficient), furin tuning (summer object, not appropriate for winter hibernation frame), koto ornamentation (not guzheng vocabulary), release ritual sound (no gong or singing bowl — Tibetan/Chinese coding, not Japanese). Audio must be treated as 18–25% of production budget, not 8–12%.

**R22: Voluntary Patronage Above Founder's Lantern Ceiling**
Add tip-jar/pay-above-floor mechanism, annual studio supporter tier, and gift-a-pond mechanic. None violate hard constraints. All serve the patronage psychology the Founder's Lantern already implicitly establishes.

</details>

---

These recommendations converge across all batch findings: the concept is novel, the team is credible, the gaps are correctable, and the hard constraints are the product's strongest differentiator — not its liability. The following section identifies supplementary domain-specific findings that did not fit the primary recommendation taxonomy but carry additional advisory weight.

# Supplementary Findings

These findings emerged from expert domains whose primary outputs did not fit the core module taxonomy but carry direct advisory weight. Each contributes evidence toward at least one of the eight open questions.

---

## S1: Historical Verdict on Three-Audience Positioning

<span class="rpt-badge">Games Historian · Q4</span>

<blockquote class="rpt-quote"><p>The marketing strategist's typical argument that multi-segment positioning at launch fails is complicated by genre history. Sky: Children of the Light successfully straddled cozy, collectible-social, and emotional/mindfulness audiences — but did so by leading with visual spectacle that collapsed the distinctions at storefront. Between Ponds leads with text and quiet, which is a harder collapse to execute.</p><footer>Games Historian · Evidence Quality: Medium</footer></blockquote>

Sky: Children of the Light (thatgamecompany, 160M+ downloads) is the reference case for three-audience positioning succeeding. The mechanism was visual spectacle: a single hero asset that made the audience-category distinction irrelevant before the user had to decide which audience they belonged to. The cherry blossom V2 pond hero shot (art/05) is Between Ponds' best attempt at this collapse — if it stops the scroll.

**The historical question** is not whether you can serve three audiences, but whether your hero asset makes the distinction irrelevant at storefront. The Release Ritual (art/01) and the Memory Wall pavilion (art/06) serve different audiences. The V2 cherry blossom pond (art/05) is the only frame that attempts to serve all three simultaneously.

**Cross-reference with marketing strategist:** The marketing strategist's likely position — that multi-segment positioning dilutes CPM targeting and produces algorithmic ambiguity — is historically valid for most cases but not categorically true. The counter-evidence is Sky. The test is whether the hero shot performs the collapse, not whether the positioning strategy names three audiences.

*See [Recommendations] R12 for the panel's final positioning verdict.*

---

## S2: GDPR Re-Identification Risk — DPIA Required

<span class="rpt-badge warning">Regulatory Compliance · Q6 · Germany</span>

The game designer will likely argue that the haiku-only constraint makes messages too generic to constitute personal data — a 17-syllable poem is not 'identifying.' This reasoning is incomplete under GDPR.

**The re-identification vector:** A haiku + city-of-origin + timestamp + breeding lineage creates a combinatorial fingerprint. GDPR Recital 26 specifies that identifiability is assessed by considering "all the means reasonably likely to be used" to identify a natural person — this is probabilistic, not binary. In cities with fewer active players (which will be most launch cities in Year 1), the fingerprint may be sufficient to identify a specific sender with moderate confidence.

**Resolution:** A Data Protection Impact Assessment (DPIA) examining re-identification risk across city-size distributions in Germany, Japan, UK, and Brazil. This is a technical exercise, not a design assumption. The assessment should model:
- Minimum player density per city at which fingerprint uniqueness drops below identifiability threshold
- Whether city-level granularity (vs. region-level) changes the analysis
- Whether koi lineage data constitutes processing of identifiable data when combined with message metadata

**Cross-reference with game designer:** The game designer's position — that the haiku constraint makes messages anonymized — cannot be the legal basis for the data model. GDPR does not accept design intent as a substitute for risk assessment.

*See [Recommendations] R2 for DPIA commissioning guidance.*

---

## S3: The Lineage Scroll as Secondary Market Antidote

<span class="rpt-badge">Narrative Designer · Q8 — Secondary Market</span>

The rare-pattern secondary market (Q8) is typically framed as a ToS enforcement problem. The narrative design perspective reframes it: **the secondary market will form precisely because the founders have not given players an adequate in-game way to celebrate and share their lineage stories.**

### The Lineage System as Unexploited Story Engine

Every rare pattern can be traced back to the strangers who made it possible. A 'moonlight lacquer' pattern only emerges when a Northern Hemisphere winter pond koi breeds with a Southern Hemisphere summer pond koi. The narrative embedded in that pattern:

> *A player in Berlin wrote a haiku in December → their koi traveled to São Paulo → a player in Brazil kept it and bred it with their summer pond koi → the resulting offspring carries the mark of two hemispheres touching.*

This is extraordinary narrative material — a heritage system encoding the history of specific cross-cultural encounters in a fish's genome. The secondary market forms not because players are greedy, but because the in-game Memory Wall has no mechanism to **narrate** the koi's genealogy. The lineage is *visible* but not *told*. Players with remarkable lineage patterns will migrate to Discord to tell that story because the game provides no space for it within the walls.

### The Lineage Scroll Solution

Build a 'lineage scroll' view that unfolds a koi's ancestry as a chain of the haiku that accompanied each generational crossing:

| Feature | Detail |
|---------|--------|
| **What it is** | A koi-ancestry view: haiku chain from each generational crossing |
| **Constraint compliance** | Reads existing data (koi lineage + associated haiku) in a new view — no hard constraint violations |
| **Monetization hook** | Cosmetic: scroll parchment styles, seal designs for lineage display |
| **Retention effect** | Gives remarkable lineage stories an in-game home, reducing Discord-migration pressure |
| **Thematic alignment** | Consistent with the entire cosmetic system philosophy |

**Cross-reference with regulatory compliance expert:** The compliance expert's likely position — that ToS enforcement is the primary intervention for secondary markets — is valid but insufficient. You cannot regulate desire away; you can redirect it by giving it an in-game home. The crux is whether the secondary market is driven by external speculative value (ToS matters) or unmet in-game narrative desire (narrative design is the primary intervention). The answer is probably both, but the narrative intervention is cheaper and more aligned with the game's philosophy.

*See [Recommendations] R17 for secondary market monitoring guidance.*

---

## S4: The Brazil Hemispheric Inversion Problem — Full Analysis

<span class="rpt-badge warning">Seasonal Event Analyst · Q5 · Q6 · Brazil</span>

Between Ponds ties core gameplay mechanics to real-world seasons. The four launch markets are hemispherically asymmetric: Germany, Japan, UK = Northern Hemisphere; Brazil = Southern Hemisphere. This asymmetry propagates through five distinct mechanics:

### Mechanics That Break Across the Equator

| Mechanic | Northern Hemisphere | Southern Hemisphere (Brazil) | Problem |
|----------|--------------------|-----------------------------|---------|
| **Breeding season peaks** | Spring March–May | Autumn March–May | Marketing campaign misrepresents product state to Brazilian players |
| **Rare pattern equinox windows** | Spring equinox = March 20 | March 20 = *autumn* equinox | Same calendar date, opposite seasonal meaning |
| **Winter Hibernation timing** | December–February (peak gaming revenue season) | June–August (Brazil's cool season) | Northern hibernation costs revenue at the industry's highest-value period; Brazilian hibernation is less catastrophic but still misaligned |
| **Hero shot (art/05)** | Cherry blossom = spring signal | Autumn 2027 Brazil launch: Brazilian players are in their spring — accurate for them; Northern players entering autumn are disconnected | Hero shot is seasonally accurate for ~4–6 weeks/year in Germany and the UK |
| **Seasonal cosmetics** | Four themes/year at €4.99 produced on Northern Hemisphere calendar | Brazilian players purchase 'summer themes' during their winter | Systematic out-of-season purchase; will appear in Brazil-specific conversion and churn data |

### Genre Precedent

Animal Crossing: New Horizons (2020) gave hemisphere choice at first launch — Southern Hemisphere options for Australian/New Zealand players. This is the established genre standard for hemisphere-aware game design. Between Ponds' automatic hemisphere detection via device timezone is mechanically similar, but the marketing and monetization calendar is designed around Northern Hemisphere rhythms.

### Business Consequence

<div class="rpt-kpi">
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat warning"><span class="kpi-value">4–6 wks</span><span class="kpi-label">Cherry blossom accuracy in Germany/UK per year</span></div>
  <div class="rpt-kpi-stat error"><span class="kpi-value">~50%</span><span class="kpi-label">Gaming revenue premium — Dec peak (Northern hibernation period)</span></div>
</div>

**Cross-reference with marketing strategist:** The marketing strategist will likely argue that Brazil is the smallest of the four launch markets by mobile game revenue and that hemispheric inversion is an acceptable trade-off. The seasonal analyst disagrees: Brazil's inclusion is explicitly for LGPD stress-testing and cultural validation — treating it as a secondary experience from day one undermines the strategic rationale for its inclusion and produces uninterpretable data.

*See [Recommendations] R13 for launch sequencing guidance and R15 for Brazil cosmetics calendar.*

---

## S5: Community Strategy Findings — Secondary Market and Moderation Architecture

<span class="rpt-badge">Community Strategy · Q8</span>

Two community strategy findings that address Q8 (secondary market) and the moderation architecture gap:

**Finding 1 — Secondary market formation timeline:** The secondary market will self-organize within 60–90 days of soft launch. Designate a team member to monitor Discord and eBay from soft-launch week 1. If trading channels emerge before full launch, trigger legal exposure re-assessment. If prices exceed €50 for rare patterns, accelerate the Lineage Scroll feature (see S3 above) and the Migration Season mechanic.

**Finding 2 — Moderation architecture:** The no-social-graph design creates moderation blindness — coordinated abuse cannot be detected at the individual message level. Solution: server-side metadata audit logs (time, routing, delivery, moderation decision hash). This preserves individual privacy while enabling network topology analysis to detect coordinated patterns. This is the architectural solution to the moderation gap; it does not require individual message inspection. Design official community infrastructure (moderated Discord) before the secondary market self-organizes — you cannot play catch-up with community norms once they are established.

*See [Recommendations] R7 for the reporting mechanism recommendation.*

---

## S6: Complex Systems Analysis — Routing Algorithm as Emergent Social Graph

<span class="rpt-badge">Physics / Complex Systems · Q7</span>

The physicist's theoretical framing provides supplementary context for the routing algorithm knowledge gap. The koi routing algorithm is not merely a technical implementation detail — it implicitly defines whether a de-facto follower graph exists in the system.

**The emergent graph problem:** If the routing algorithm uses any persistent player-to-player preference signals (repeat delivery weighting, affinity scoring), it creates a shadow social graph indistinguishable in effect from the follower graph the hard constraints explicitly prohibit. The constraint "No profiles, no usernames, no follower graph" is violated by implementation, not by design intent, if the routing algorithm develops persistent routing preferences.

**Safe routing architectures:** Routing that selects from a pool of qualifying players (hemisphere-appropriate, age-appropriate, activity-appropriate) without retaining per-pair routing history avoids the emergent graph problem. Document the choice explicitly before development begins.

*This finding directly informs Knowledge Gap 2 (routing algorithm specification) and cross-references with [Recommendations] R11.*
